<p class="line" name=2.2.175>May I never</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.176>To this good purpose, that so fairly shows,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.177>Dream of impediment! Let me have thy hand:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.178>Further this act of grace: and from this hour</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.179>The heart of brothers govern in our loves</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.180>And sway our great designs!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.181>There is my hand.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.182>A sister I bequeath you, whom no brother</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.183>Did ever love so dearly: let her live</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.184>To join our kingdoms and our hearts; and never</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.185>Fly off our loves again!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.186>Happily, amen!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.187>I did not think to draw my sword 'gainst Pompey;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.188>For he hath laid strange courtesies and great</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.189>Of late upon me: I must thank him only,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.190>Lest my remembrance suffer ill report;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.191>At heel of that, defy him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.192>Time calls upon's:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.193>Of us must Pompey presently be sought,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.194>Or else he seeks out us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.195>Where lies he?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.196>About the mount Misenum.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.197>What is his strength by land?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.198>Great and increasing: but by sea</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.199>He is an absolute master.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.200>So is the fame.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.201>Would we had spoke together! Haste we for it:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.202>Yet, ere we put ourselves in arms, dispatch we</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.203>The business we have talk'd of.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.204>With most gladness:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.205>And do invite you to my sister's view,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.206>Whither straight I'll lead you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.207>Let us, Lepidus,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.208>Not lack your company.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.209>Noble Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.210>Not sickness should detain me.</p>
<p><i>Flourish. Exeunt OCTAVIUS CAESAR, MARK ANTONY, and LEPIDUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.211>Welcome from Egypt, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.212>Half the heart of Caesar, worthy Mecaenas! My</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.213>honourable friend, Agrippa!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.214>Good Enobarbus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.215>We have cause to be glad that matters are so well</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.216>digested. You stayed well by 't in Egypt.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.217>Ay, sir; we did sleep day out of countenance, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.218>made the night light with drinking.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.219>Eight wild-boars roasted whole at a breakfast, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.220>but twelve persons there; is this true?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.221>This was but as a fly by an eagle: we had much more</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.222>monstrous matter of feast, which worthily deserved noting.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.223>She's a most triumphant lady, if report be square to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.224>her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.225>When she first met Mark Antony, she pursed up</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.226>his heart, upon the river of Cydnus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.227>There she appeared indeed; or my reporter devised</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.228>well for her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.229>I will tell you.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.230>The barge she sat in, like a burnish'd throne,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.231>Burn'd on the water: the poop was beaten gold;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.232>Purple the sails, and so perfumed that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.233>The winds were love-sick with them; the oars were silver,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.234>Which to the tune of flutes kept stroke, and made</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.235>The water which they beat to follow faster,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.236>As amorous of their strokes. For her own person,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.237>It beggar'd all description: she did lie</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.238>In her pavilion--cloth-of-gold of tissue--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.239>O'er-picturing that Venus where we see</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.240>The fancy outwork nature: on each side her</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.241>Stood pretty dimpled boys, like smiling Cupids,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.242>With divers-colour'd fans, whose wind did seem</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.243>To glow the delicate cheeks which they did cool,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.244>And what they undid did.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.245>O, rare for Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.246>Her gentlewomen, like the Nereides,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.247>So many mermaids, tended her i' the eyes,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.248>And made their bends adornings: at the helm</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.249>A seeming mermaid steers: the silken tackle</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.250>Swell with the touches of those flower-soft hands,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.251>That yarely frame the office. From the barge</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.252>A strange invisible perfume hits the sense</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.253>Of the adjacent wharfs. The city cast</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.254>Her people out upon her; and Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.255>Enthroned i' the market-place, did sit alone,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.256>Whistling to the air; which, but for vacancy,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.257>Had gone to gaze on Cleopatra too,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.258>And made a gap in nature.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.259>Rare Egyptian!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.260>Upon her landing, Antony sent to her,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.261>Invited her to supper: she replied,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.262>It should be better he became her guest;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.263>Which she entreated: our courteous Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.264>Whom ne'er the word of 'No' woman heard speak,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.265>Being barber'd ten times o'er, goes to the feast,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.266>And for his ordinary pays his heart</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.267>For what his eyes eat only.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.268>Royal wench!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.269>She made great Caesar lay his sword to bed:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.270>He plough'd her, and she cropp'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.271>I saw her once</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.272>Hop forty paces through the public street;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.273>And having lost her breath, she spoke, and panted,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.274>That she did make defect perfection,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.275>And, breathless, power breathe forth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.276>Now Antony must leave her utterly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.277>Never; he will not:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.278>Age cannot wither her, nor custom stale</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.279>Her infinite variety: other women cloy</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.280>The appetites they feed: but she makes hungry</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.281>Where most she satisfies; for vilest things</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.282>Become themselves in her: that the holy priests</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.283>Bless her when she is riggish.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.284>If beauty, wisdom, modesty, can settle</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.285>The heart of Antony, Octavia is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.286>A blessed lottery to him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.287>Let us go.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.288>Good Enobarbus, make yourself my guest</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.289>Whilst you abide here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.290>Humbly, sir, I thank you.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. The same. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY, OCTAVIUS CAESAR, OCTAVIA between them, and Attendants</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.1>The world and my great office will sometimes</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.2>Divide me from your bosom.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.3>All which time</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.4>Before the gods my knee shall bow my prayers</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.5>To them for you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.6>                  Good night, sir. My Octavia,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.7>Read not my blemishes in the world's report:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.8>I have not kept my square; but that to come</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.9>Shall all be done by the rule. Good night, dear lady.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.10>Good night, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.11>Good night.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt OCTAVIUS CAESAR and OCTAVIA</i></p>
<p><i>Enter Soothsayer</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.12>Now, sirrah; you do wish yourself in Egypt?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.13>Would I had never come from thence, nor you Thither!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.14>If you can, your reason?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.15>I see it in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.16>My motion, have it not in my tongue: but yet</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.17>Hie you to Egypt again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.18>Say to me,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.19>Whose fortunes shall rise higher, Caesar's or mine?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.20>Caesar's.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.21>Therefore, O Antony, stay not by his side:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.22>Thy demon, that's thy spirit which keeps thee, is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.23>Noble, courageous high, unmatchable,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.24>Where Caesar's is not; but, near him, thy angel</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.25>Becomes a fear, as being o'erpower'd: therefore</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.26>Make space enough between you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.27>Speak this no more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Soothsayer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.28>To none but thee; no more, but when to thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.29>If thou dost play with him at any game,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.30>Thou art sure to lose; and, of that natural luck,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.31>He beats thee 'gainst the odds: thy lustre thickens,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.32>When he shines by: I say again, thy spirit</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.33>Is all afraid to govern thee near him;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.34>But, he away, 'tis noble.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.35>Get thee gone:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.36>Say to Ventidius I would speak with him:</p>
<p><i>Exit Soothsayer</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.37>He shall to Parthia. Be it art or hap,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.38>He hath spoken true: the very dice obey him;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.39>And in our sports my better cunning faints</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.40>Under his chance: if we draw lots, he speeds;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.41>His cocks do win the battle still of mine,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.42>When it is all to nought; and his quails ever</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.43>Beat mine, inhoop'd, at odds. I will to Egypt:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.44>And though I make this marriage for my peace,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.45>I' the east my pleasure lies.</p>
<p><i>Enter VENTIDIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.46>O, come, Ventidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.47>You must to Parthia: your commission's ready;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.48>Follow me, and receive't.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. The same. A street.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter LEPIDUS, MECAENAS, and AGRIPPA</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.1>Trouble yourselves no further: pray you, hasten</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.2>Your generals after.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.3>Sir, Mark Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.4>Will e'en but kiss Octavia, and we'll follow.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.5>Till I shall see you in your soldier's dress,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.6>Which will become you both, farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.7>We shall,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.8>As I conceive the journey, be at the Mount</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.9>Before you, Lepidus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.10>Your way is shorter;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.11>My purposes do draw me much about:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.4.12>You'll win two days upon me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>MECAENAS</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.13>Sir, good success!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.4.14>Farewell.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE V. Alexandria. CLEOPATRA's palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA, CHARMIAN, IRAS, and ALEXAS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.1>Give me some music; music, moody food</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.2>Of us that trade in love.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Attendants</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.3>The music, ho!</p>
<p><i>Enter MARDIAN</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.4>Let it alone; let's to billiards: come, Charmian.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.5>My arm is sore; best play with Mardian.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.6>As well a woman with an eunuch play'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.7>As with a woman. Come, you'll play with me, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>MARDIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.8>As well as I can, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.9>And when good will is show'd, though't come</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.10>too short,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.11>The actor may plead pardon. I'll none now:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.12>Give me mine angle; we'll to the river: there,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.13>My music playing far off, I will betray</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.14>Tawny-finn'd fishes; my bended hook shall pierce</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.15>Their slimy jaws; and, as I draw them up,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.16>I'll think them every one an Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.17>And say 'Ah, ha! you're caught.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.18>'Twas merry when</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.19>You wager'd on your angling; when your diver</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.20>Did hang a salt-fish on his hook, which he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.21>With fervency drew up.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.22>That time,--O times!--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.23>I laugh'd him out of patience; and that night</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.24>I laugh'd him into patience; and next morn,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.25>Ere the ninth hour, I drunk him to his bed;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.26>Then put my tires and mantles on him, whilst</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.27>I wore his sword Philippan.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.28>O, from Italy</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.29>Ram thou thy fruitful tidings in mine ears,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.30>That long time have been barren.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.31>Madam, madam,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.32>Antonius dead!--If thou say so, villain,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.33>Thou kill'st thy mistress: but well and free,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.34>If thou so yield him, there is gold, and here</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.35>My bluest veins to kiss; a hand that kings</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.36>Have lipp'd, and trembled kissing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.37>First, madam, he is well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.38>Why, there's more gold.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.39>But, sirrah, mark, we use</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.40>To say the dead are well: bring it to that,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.41>The gold I give thee will I melt and pour</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.42>Down thy ill-uttering throat.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.43>Good madam, hear me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.44>Well, go to, I will;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.45>But there's no goodness in thy face: if Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.46>Be free and healthful,--so tart a favour</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.47>To trumpet such good tidings! If not well,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.48>Thou shouldst come like a Fury crown'd with snakes,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.49>Not like a formal man.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.50>Will't please you hear me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.51>I have a mind to strike thee ere thou speak'st:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.52>Yet if thou say Antony lives, is well,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.53>Or friends with Caesar, or not captive to him,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.54>I'll set thee in a shower of gold, and hail</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.55>Rich pearls upon thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.56>Madam, he's well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.57>Well said.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.58>And friends with Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.59>Thou'rt an honest man.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.60>Caesar and he are greater friends than ever.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.61>Make thee a fortune from me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.62>But yet, madam,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.63>I do not like 'But yet,' it does allay</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.64>The good precedence; fie upon 'But yet'!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.65>'But yet' is as a gaoler to bring forth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.66>Some monstrous malefactor. Prithee, friend,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.67>Pour out the pack of matter to mine ear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.68>The good and bad together: he's friends with Caesar:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.69>In state of health thou say'st; and thou say'st free.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.70>Free, madam! no; I made no such report:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.71>He's bound unto Octavia.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.72>For what good turn?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.73>For the best turn i' the bed.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.74>I am pale, Charmian.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.75>Madam, he's married to Octavia.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.76>The most infectious pestilence upon thee!</p>
<p><i>Strikes him down</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.77>Good madam, patience.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.78>What say you? Hence,</p>
<p><i>Strikes him again</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.79>Horrible villain! or I'll spurn thine eyes</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.80>Like balls before me; I'll unhair thy head:</p>
<p><i>She hales him up and down</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.81>Thou shalt be whipp'd with wire, and stew'd in brine,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.82>Smarting in lingering pickle.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.83>Gracious madam,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.84>I that do bring the news made not the match.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.85>Say 'tis not so, a province I will give thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.86>And make thy fortunes proud: the blow thou hadst</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.87>Shall make thy peace for moving me to rage;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.88>And I will boot thee with what gift beside</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.89>Thy modesty can beg.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.90>He's married, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.91>Rogue, thou hast lived too long.</p>
<p><i>Draws a knife</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.92>Nay, then I'll run.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.93>What mean you, madam? I have made no fault.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.94>Good madam, keep yourself within yourself:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.95>The man is innocent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.96>Some innocents 'scape not the thunderbolt.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.97>Melt Egypt into Nile! and kindly creatures</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.98>Turn all to serpents! Call the slave again:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.99>Though I am mad, I will not bite him: call.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.100>He is afeard to come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.101>I will not hurt him.</p>
<p><i>Exit CHARMIAN</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.102>These hands do lack nobility, that they strike</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.103>A meaner than myself; since I myself</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.104>Have given myself the cause.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter CHARMIAN and Messenger</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.105>Come hither, sir.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.106>Though it be honest, it is never good</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.107>To bring bad news: give to a gracious message.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.108>An host of tongues; but let ill tidings tell</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.109>Themselves when they be felt.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.110>I have done my duty.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.111>Is he married?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.112>I cannot hate thee worser than I do,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.113>If thou again say 'Yes.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.114>He's married, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.115>The gods confound thee! dost thou hold there still?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.116>Should I lie, madam?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.117>O, I would thou didst,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.118>So half my Egypt were submerged and made</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.119>A cistern for scaled snakes! Go, get thee hence:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.120>Hadst thou Narcissus in thy face, to me</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.121>Thou wouldst appear most ugly. He is married?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.122>I crave your highness' pardon.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.123>He is married?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.124>Take no offence that I would not offend you:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.125>To punish me for what you make me do.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.126>Seems much unequal: he's married to Octavia.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.127>O, that his fault should make a knave of thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.128>That art not what thou'rt sure of! Get thee hence:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.129>The merchandise which thou hast brought from Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.130>Are all too dear for me: lie they upon thy hand,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.131>And be undone by 'em!</p>
<p><i>Exit Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.132>Good your highness, patience.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.133>In praising Antony, I have dispraised Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.134>Many times, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.5.135>                  I am paid for't now.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.136>Lead me from hence:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.137>I faint: O Iras, Charmian! 'tis no matter.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.138>Go to the fellow, good Alexas; bid him</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.139>Report the feature of Octavia, her years,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.140>Her inclination, let him not leave out</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.141>The colour of her hair: bring me word quickly.</p>
<p><i>Exit ALEXAS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.142>Let him for ever go:--let him not--Charmian,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.143>Though he be painted one way like a Gorgon,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.144>The other way's a Mars. Bid you Alexas</p>
<p><i>To MARDIAN</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.145>Bring me word how tall she is. Pity me, Charmian,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.5.146>But do not speak to me. Lead me to my chamber.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VI. Near Misenum.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Flourish. Enter POMPEY and MENAS at one door,  with drum and trumpet: at another, OCTAVIUS CAESAR,  MARK ANTONY, LEPIDUS, DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS, MECAENAS, with Soldiers marching</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.1>Your hostages I have, so have you mine;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.2>And we shall talk before we fight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.3>Most meet</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.4>That first we come to words; and therefore have we</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.5>Our written purposes before us sent;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.6>Which, if thou hast consider'd, let us know</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.7>If 'twill tie up thy discontented sword,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.8>And carry back to Sicily much tall youth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.9>That else must perish here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.10>To you all three,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.11>The senators alone of this great world,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.12>Chief factors for the gods, I do not know</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.13>Wherefore my father should revengers want,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.14>Having a son and friends; since Julius Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.15>Who at Philippi the good Brutus ghosted,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.16>There saw you labouring for him. What was't</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.17>That moved pale Cassius to conspire; and what</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.18>Made the all-honour'd, honest Roman, Brutus,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.19>With the arm'd rest, courtiers and beauteous freedom,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.20>To drench the Capitol; but that they would</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.21>Have one man but a man? And that is it</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.22>Hath made me rig my navy; at whose burthen</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.23>The anger'd ocean foams; with which I meant</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.24>To scourge the ingratitude that despiteful Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.25>Cast on my noble father.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.26>Take your time.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.27>Thou canst not fear us, Pompey, with thy sails;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.28>We'll speak with thee at sea: at land, thou know'st</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.29>How much we do o'er-count thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.30>At land, indeed,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.31>Thou dost o'er-count me of my father's house:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.32>But, since the cuckoo builds not for himself,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.33>Remain in't as thou mayst.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.34>Be pleased to tell us--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.35>For this is from the present--how you take</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.36>The offers we have sent you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.37>There's the point.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.38>Which do not be entreated to, but weigh</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.39>What it is worth embraced.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.40>And what may follow,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.41>To try a larger fortune.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.42>You have made me offer</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.43>Of Sicily, Sardinia; and I must</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.44>Rid all the sea of pirates; then, to send</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.45>Measures of wheat to Rome; this 'greed upon</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.46>To part with unhack'd edges, and bear back</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.47>Our targes undinted.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.48>That's our offer.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.49>Know, then,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.50>I came before you here a man prepared</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.51>To take this offer: but Mark Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.52>Put me to some impatience: though I lose</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.53>The praise of it by telling, you must know,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.54>When Caesar and your brother were at blows,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.55>Your mother came to Sicily and did find</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.56>Her welcome friendly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.57>I have heard it, Pompey;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.58>And am well studied for a liberal thanks</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.59>Which I do owe you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.60>Let me have your hand:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.61>I did not think, sir, to have met you here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.62>The beds i' the east are soft; and thanks to you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.63>That call'd me timelier than my purpose hither;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.64>For I have gain'd by 't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.65>Since I saw you last,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.66>There is a change upon you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.67>Well, I know not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.68>What counts harsh fortune casts upon my face;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.69>But in my bosom shall she never come,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.70>To make my heart her vassal.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.71>Well met here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.72>I hope so, Lepidus. Thus we are agreed:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.73>I crave our composition may be written,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.74>And seal'd between us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.75>That's the next to do.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.76>We'll feast each other ere we part; and let's</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.77>Draw lots who shall begin.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.78>That will I, Pompey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.79>No, Antony, take the lot: but, first</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.80>Or last, your fine Egyptian cookery</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.81>Shall have the fame. I have heard that Julius Caesar</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.82>Grew fat with feasting there.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.83>You have heard much.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.84>I have fair meanings, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.85>And fair words to them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.86>Then so much have I heard:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.87>And I have heard, Apollodorus carried--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.88>No more of that: he did so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.89>What, I pray you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.90>A certain queen to Caesar in a mattress.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.91>I know thee now: how farest thou, soldier?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.92>Well;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.93>And well am like to do; for, I perceive,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.94>Four feasts are toward.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.95>Let me shake thy hand;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.96>I never hated thee: I have seen thee fight,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.97>When I have envied thy behavior.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.98>Sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.99>I never loved you much; but I ha' praised ye,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.100>When you have well deserved ten times as much</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.101>As I have said you did.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.102>Enjoy thy plainness,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.103>It nothing ill becomes thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.104>Aboard my galley I invite you all:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.105>Will you lead, lords?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.106>Show us the way, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.107>Come.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but MENAS and ENOBARBUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.108>[Aside]  Thy father, Pompey, would ne'er have</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.109>made this treaty.--You and I have known, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.110>At sea, I think.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.111>We have, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.112>You have done well by water.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.113>And you by land.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.114>I will praise any man that will praise me; though it</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.115>cannot be denied what I have done by land.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.116>Nor what I have done by water.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.117>Yes, something you can deny for your own</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.118>safety: you have been a great thief by sea.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.119>And you by land.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.120>There I deny my land service. But give me your</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.121>hand, Menas: if our eyes had authority, here they</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.122>might take two thieves kissing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.123>All men's faces are true, whatsome'er their hands are.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.124>But there is never a fair woman has a true face.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.125>No slander; they steal hearts.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.126>We came hither to fight with you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.127>For my part, I am sorry it is turned to a drinking.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.128>Pompey doth this day laugh away his fortune.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.129>If he do, sure, he cannot weep't back again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.130>You've said, sir. We looked not for Mark Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.131>here: pray you, is he married to Cleopatra?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.132>Caesar's sister is called Octavia.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.133>True, sir; she was the wife of Caius Marcellus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.134>But she is now the wife of Marcus Antonius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.135>Pray ye, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.136>'Tis true.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.137>Then is Caesar and he for ever knit together.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.138>If I were bound to divine of this unity, I would</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.139>not prophesy so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.140>I think the policy of that purpose made more in the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.141>marriage than the love of the parties.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.142>I think so too. But you shall find, the band that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.143>seems to tie their friendship together will be the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.144>very strangler of their amity: Octavia is of a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.145>holy, cold, and still conversation.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.146>Who would not have his wife so?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.147>Not he that himself is not so; which is Mark Antony.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.148>He will to his Egyptian dish again: then shall the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.149>sighs of Octavia blow the fire up in Caesar; and, as</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.150>I said before, that which is the strength of their</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.151>amity shall prove the immediate author of their</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.152>variance. Antony will use his affection where it is:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.153>he married but his occasion here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.154>And thus it may be. Come, sir, will you aboard?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.6.155>I have a health for you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.156>I shall take it, sir: we have used our throats in Egypt.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.6.157>Come, let's away.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VII. On board POMPEY's galley, off Misenum.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Music plays. Enter two or three Servants with a banquet</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.1>Here they'll be, man. Some o' their plants are</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.2>ill-rooted already: the least wind i' the world</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.3>will blow them down.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.4>Lepidus is high-coloured.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>First Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.5>They have made him drink alms-drink.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Second Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.6>As they pinch one another by the disposition, he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.7>cries out 'No more;' reconciles them to his</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.8>entreaty, and himself to the drink.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>First Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.9>But it raises the greater war between him and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.10>his discretion.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Second Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.11>Why, this is to have a name in great men's</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.12>fellowship: I had as lief have a reed that will do</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.13>me no service as a partisan I could not heave.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>First Servant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.14>To be called into a huge sphere, and not to be seen</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.15>to move in't, are the holes where eyes should be,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.16>which pitifully disaster the cheeks.</p>
<p><i>A sennet sounded. Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, MARK  ANTONY, LEPIDUS, POMPEY, AGRIPPA, MECAENAS, DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS, MENAS, with other captains</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.17>[To OCTAVIUS CAESAR]  Thus do they, sir: they take</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.18>the flow o' the Nile</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.19>By certain scales i' the pyramid; they know,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.20>By the height, the lowness, or the mean, if dearth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.21>Or foison follow: the higher Nilus swells,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.22>The more it promises: as it ebbs, the seedsman</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.23>Upon the slime and ooze scatters his grain,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.24>And shortly comes to harvest.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.25>You've strange serpents there.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.26>Ay, Lepidus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.27>Your serpent of Egypt is bred now of your mud by the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.28>operation of your sun: so is your crocodile.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.29>They are so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.30>Sit,--and some wine! A health to Lepidus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.31>I am not so well as I should be, but I'll ne'er out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.32>Not till you have slept; I fear me you'll be in till then.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.33>Nay, certainly, I have heard the Ptolemies'</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.34>pyramises are very goodly things; without</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.35>contradiction, I have heard that.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.36>[Aside to POMPEY]  Pompey, a word.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.37>[Aside to MENAS]                 Say in mine ear:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.38>what is't?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.39>[Aside to POMPEY]  Forsake thy seat, I do beseech</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.40>thee, captain,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.41>And hear me speak a word.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.42>[Aside to MENAS]  Forbear me till anon.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.43>This wine for Lepidus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.44>What manner o' thing is your crocodile?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.45>It is shaped, sir, like itself; and it is as broad</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.46>as it hath breadth: it is just so high as it is,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.47>and moves with its own organs: it lives by that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.48>which nourisheth it; and the elements once out of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.49>it, it transmigrates.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.50>What colour is it of?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.51>Of it own colour too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.52>'Tis a strange serpent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.53>'Tis so. And the tears of it are wet.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.54>Will this description satisfy him?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.55>With the health that Pompey gives him, else he is a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.56>very epicure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.57>[Aside to MENAS]  Go hang, sir, hang! Tell me of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.58>that? away!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.59>Do as I bid you. Where's this cup I call'd for?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.60>[Aside to POMPEY]  If for the sake of merit thou</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.61>wilt hear me,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.62>Rise from thy stool.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.63>[Aside to MENAS]  I think thou'rt mad.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.64>The matter?</p>
<p><i>Rises, and walks aside</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.65>I have ever held my cap off to thy fortunes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.66>Thou hast served me with much faith. What's else to say?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.67>Be jolly, lords.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.68>                  These quick-sands, Lepidus,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.69>Keep off them, for you sink.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.70>Wilt thou be lord of all the world?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.71>What say'st thou?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.72>Wilt thou be lord of the whole world? That's twice.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.73>How should that be?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.74>But entertain it,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.75>And, though thou think me poor, I am the man</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.76>Will give thee all the world.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.77>Hast thou drunk well?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.78>Now, Pompey, I have kept me from the cup.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.79>Thou art, if thou darest be, the earthly Jove:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.80>Whate'er the ocean pales, or sky inclips,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.81>Is thine, if thou wilt ha't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.82>Show me which way.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.83>These three world-sharers, these competitors,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.84>Are in thy vessel: let me cut the cable;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.85>And, when we are put off, fall to their throats:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.86>All there is thine.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.87>Ah, this thou shouldst have done,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.88>And not have spoke on't! In me 'tis villany;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.89>In thee't had been good service. Thou must know,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.90>'Tis not my profit that does lead mine honour;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.91>Mine honour, it. Repent that e'er thy tongue</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.92>Hath so betray'd thine act: being done unknown,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.93>I should have found it afterwards well done;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.94>But must condemn it now. Desist, and drink.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.95>[Aside]  For this,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.96>I'll never follow thy pall'd fortunes more.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.97>Who seeks, and will not take when once 'tis offer'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.98>Shall never find it more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.99>This health to Lepidus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.100>Bear him ashore. I'll pledge it for him, Pompey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.101>Here's to thee, Menas!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.102>Enobarbus, welcome!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.103>Fill till the cup be hid.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.104>There's a strong fellow, Menas.</p>
<p><i>Pointing to the Attendant who carries off LEPIDUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.105>Why?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.106>A' bears the third part of the world, man; see'st</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.107>not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.108>The third part, then, is drunk: would it were all,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.109>That it might go on wheels!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.110>Drink thou; increase the reels.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.111>Come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.112>This is not yet an Alexandrian feast.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.113>It ripens towards it. Strike the vessels, ho?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.114>Here is to Caesar!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.115>                  I could well forbear't.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.116>It's monstrous labour, when I wash my brain,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.117>And it grows fouler.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.118>Be a child o' the time.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.119>Possess it, I'll make answer:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.120>But I had rather fast from all four days</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.121>Than drink so much in one.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.122>Ha, my brave emperor!</p>
<p><i>To MARK ANTONY</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.123>Shall we dance now the Egyptian Bacchanals,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.124>And celebrate our drink?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.125>Let's ha't, good soldier.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.126>Come, let's all take hands,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.127>Till that the conquering wine hath steep'd our sense</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.128>In soft and delicate Lethe.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.129>All take hands.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.130>Make battery to our ears with the loud music:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.131>The while I'll place you: then the boy shall sing;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.132>The holding every man shall bear as loud</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.133>As his strong sides can volley.</p>
<p><i>Music plays. DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS places them hand in hand</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.134>THE SONG.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.135>Come, thou monarch of the vine,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.136>Plumpy Bacchus with pink eyne!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.137>In thy fats our cares be drown'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.138>With thy grapes our hairs be crown'd:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.139>Cup us, till the world go round,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.140>Cup us, till the world go round!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.141>What would you more? Pompey, good night. Good brother,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.142>Let me request you off: our graver business</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.143>Frowns at this levity. Gentle lords, let's part;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.144>You see we have burnt our cheeks: strong Enobarb</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.145>Is weaker than the wine; and mine own tongue</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.146>Splits what it speaks: the wild disguise hath almost</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.147>Antick'd us all. What needs more words? Good night.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.148>Good Antony, your hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.149>I'll try you on the shore.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.150>And shall, sir; give's your hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>POMPEY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.151>O Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.152>You have my father's house,--But, what? we are friends.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.153>Come, down into the boat.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.154>Take heed you fall not.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS and MENAS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.155>Menas, I'll not on shore.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.156>No, to my cabin.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.157>These drums! these trumpets, flutes! what!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.158>Let Neptune hear we bid a loud farewell</p>
<p class="line" name=2.7.159>To these great fellows: sound and be hang'd, sound out!</p>
<p><i>Sound a flourish, with drums</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.160>Ho! says a' There's my cap.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>MENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.7.161>Ho! Noble captain, come.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT III</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. A plain in Syria.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter VENTIDIUS as it were in triumph, with SILIUS,  and other Romans, Officers, and Soldiers; the dead body of PACORUS borne before him</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>VENTIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.1>Now, darting Parthia, art thou struck; and now</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.2>Pleased fortune does of Marcus Crassus' death</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.3>Make me revenger. Bear the king's son's body</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.4>Before our army. Thy Pacorus, Orodes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.5>Pays this for Marcus Crassus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>SILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.6>Noble Ventidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.7>Whilst yet with Parthian blood thy sword is warm,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.8>The fugitive Parthians follow; spur through Media,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.9>Mesopotamia, and the shelters whither</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.10>The routed fly: so thy grand captain Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.11>Shall set thee on triumphant chariots and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.12>Put garlands on thy head.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>VENTIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.13>O Silius, Silius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.14>I have done enough; a lower place, note well,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.15>May make too great an act: for learn this, Silius;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.16>Better to leave undone, than by our deed</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.17>Acquire too high a fame when him we serve's away.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.18>Caesar and Antony have ever won</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.19>More in their officer than person: Sossius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.20>One of my place in Syria, his lieutenant,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.21>For quick accumulation of renown,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.22>Which he achieved by the minute, lost his favour.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.23>Who does i' the wars more than his captain can</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.24>Becomes his captain's captain: and ambition,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.25>The soldier's virtue, rather makes choice of loss,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.26>Than gain which darkens him.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.27>I could do more to do Antonius good,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.28>But 'twould offend him; and in his offence</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.29>Should my performance perish.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>SILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.30>Thou hast, Ventidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.31>that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.32>Without the which a soldier, and his sword,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.33>Grants scarce distinction. Thou wilt write to Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>VENTIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.34>I'll humbly signify what in his name,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.35>That magical word of war, we have effected;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.36>How, with his banners and his well-paid ranks,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.37>The ne'er-yet-beaten horse of Parthia</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.38>We have jaded out o' the field.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>SILIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.39>Where is he now?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>VENTIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.40>He purposeth to Athens: whither, with what haste</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.41>The weight we must convey with's will permit,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.42>We shall appear before him. On there; pass along!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. Rome. An ante-chamber in OCTAVIUS CAESAR's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter AGRIPPA at one door, DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS at another</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.1>What, are the brothers parted?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.2>They have dispatch'd with Pompey, he is gone;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.3>The other three are sealing. Octavia weeps</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.4>To part from Rome; Caesar is sad; and Lepidus,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.5>Since Pompey's feast, as Menas says, is troubled</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.6>With the green sickness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.7>'Tis a noble Lepidus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.8>A very fine one: O, how he loves Caesar!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.9>Nay, but how dearly he adores Mark Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.10>Caesar? Why, he's the Jupiter of men.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.11>What's Antony? The god of Jupiter.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.12>Spake you of Caesar? How! the non-pareil!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.13>O Antony! O thou Arabian bird!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.14>Would you praise Caesar, say 'Caesar:' go no further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.15>Indeed, he plied them both with excellent praises.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.16>But he loves Caesar best; yet he loves Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.17>Ho! hearts, tongues, figures, scribes, bards,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.18>poets, cannot</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.19>Think, speak, cast, write, sing, number, ho!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.20>His love to Antony. But as for Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.21>Kneel down, kneel down, and wonder.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.22>Both he loves.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.23>They are his shards, and he their beetle.</p>
<p><i>Trumpets within</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.24>So;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.25>This is to horse. Adieu, noble Agrippa.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.26>Good fortune, worthy soldier; and farewell.</p>
<p><i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, MARK ANTONY, LEPIDUS, and OCTAVIA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.27>No further, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.28>You take from me a great part of myself;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.29>Use me well in 't. Sister, prove such a wife</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.30>As my thoughts make thee, and as my farthest band</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.31>Shall pass on thy approof. Most noble Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.32>Let not the piece of virtue, which is set</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.33>Betwixt us as the cement of our love,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.34>To keep it builded, be the ram to batter</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.35>The fortress of it; for better might we</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.36>Have loved without this mean, if on both parts</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.37>This be not cherish'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.38>Make me not offended</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.39>In your distrust.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.40>                  I have said.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.41>You shall not find,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.42>Though you be therein curious, the least cause</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.43>For what you seem to fear: so, the gods keep you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.44>And make the hearts of Romans serve your ends!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.45>We will here part.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.46>Farewell, my dearest sister, fare thee well:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.47>The elements be kind to thee, and make</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.48>Thy spirits all of comfort! fare thee well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.49>My noble brother!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.50>The April 's in her eyes: it is love's spring,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.51>And these the showers to bring it on. Be cheerful.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.52>Sir, look well to my husband's house; and--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.53>What, Octavia?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.54>       I'll tell you in your ear.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.55>Her tongue will not obey her heart, nor can</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.56>Her heart inform her tongue,--the swan's</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.57>down-feather,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.58>That stands upon the swell at full of tide,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.59>And neither way inclines.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.60>[Aside to AGRIPPA]  Will Caesar weep?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.61>[Aside to DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS]  He has a cloud in 's face.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.62>[Aside to AGRIPPA]  He were the worse for that,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.63>were he a horse;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.64>So is he, being a man.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.65>[Aside to DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS]  Why, Enobarbus,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.66>When Antony found Julius Caesar dead,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.67>He cried almost to roaring; and he wept</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.68>When at Philippi he found Brutus slain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.69>[Aside to AGRIPPA]  That year, indeed, he was</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.70>troubled with a rheum;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.71>What willingly he did confound he wail'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.72>Believe't, till I wept too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.73>No, sweet Octavia,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.74>You shall hear from me still; the time shall not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.75>Out-go my thinking on you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.76>Come, sir, come;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.77>I'll wrestle with you in my strength of love:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.78>Look, here I have you; thus I let you go,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.79>And give you to the gods.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.80>Adieu; be happy!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>LEPIDUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.81>Let all the number of the stars give light</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.82>To thy fair way!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.83>Farewell, fa rewell!</p>
<p><i>Kisses OCTAVIA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.84>Farewell!</p>
<p><i>Trumpets sound. Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. Alexandria. CLEOPATRA's palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA, CHARMIAN, IRAS, and ALEXAS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.1>Where is the fellow?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>ALEXAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.2>Half afeard to come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.3>Go to, go to.</p>
<p><i>Enter the Messenger as before</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.4>Come hither, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>ALEXAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.5>Good majesty,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.6>Herod of Jewry dare not look upon you</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.7>But when you are well pleased.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.8>That Herod's head</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.9>I'll have: but how, when Antony is gone</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.10>Through whom I might command it? Come thou near.</p>
</blockquote>
