<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.11>Most gracious majesty,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.12>Didst thou behold Octavia?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.13>Ay, dread queen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.14>Where?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.15>Madam, in Rome;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.16>I look'd her in the face, and saw her led</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.17>Between her brother and Mark Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.18>Is she as tall as me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.19>She is not, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.20>Didst hear her speak? is she shrill-tongued or low?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.21>Madam, I heard her speak; she is low-voiced.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.22>That's not so good: he cannot like her long.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.23>Like her! O Isis! 'tis impossible.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.24>I think so, Charmian: dull of tongue, and dwarfish!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.25>What majesty is in her gait? Remember,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.26>If e'er thou look'dst on majesty.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.27>She creeps:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.28>Her motion and her station are as one;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.29>She shows a body rather than a life,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.30>A statue than a breather.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.31>Is this certain?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.32>Or I have no observance.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.33>Three in Egypt</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.34>Cannot make better note.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.35>He's very knowing;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.36>I do perceive't: there's nothing in her yet:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.37>The fellow has good judgment.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.38>Excellent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.39>Guess at her years, I prithee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.40>Madam,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.41>She was a widow,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.42>                  Widow! Charmian, hark.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.43>And I do think she's thirty.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.44>Bear'st thou her face in mind? is't long or round?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.45>Round even to faultiness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.46>For the most part, too, they are foolish that are so.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.47>Her hair, what colour?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.48>Brown, madam: and her forehead</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.49>As low as she would wish it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.50>There's gold for thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.51>Thou must not take my former sharpness ill:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.52>I will employ thee back again; I find thee</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.53>Most fit for business: go make thee ready;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.54>Our letters are prepared.</p>
<p><i>Exit Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.55>A proper man.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.56>Indeed, he is so: I repent me much</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.57>That so I harried him. Why, methinks, by him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.58>This creature's no such thing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.59>Nothing, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.60>The man hath seen some majesty, and should know.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.61>Hath he seen majesty? Isis else defend,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.62>And serving you so long!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.63>I have one thing more to ask him yet, good Charmian:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.64>But 'tis no matter; thou shalt bring him to me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.65>Where I will write. All may be well enough.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.66>I warrant you, madam.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. Athens. A room in MARK ANTONY's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY and OCTAVIA</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.4.1>Nay, nay, Octavia, not only that,--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.2>That were excusable, that, and thousands more</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.3>Of semblable import,--but he hath waged</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.4>New wars 'gainst Pompey; made his will, and read it</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.5>To public ear:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.6>Spoke scantly of me: when perforce he could not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.7>But pay me terms of honour, cold and sickly</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.8>He vented them; most narrow measure lent me:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.9>When the best hint was given him, he not took't,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.10>Or did it from his teeth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.4.11>O my good lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.12>Believe not all; or, if you must believe,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.13>Stomach not all. A more unhappy lady,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.14>If this division chance, ne'er stood between,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.15>Praying for both parts:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.16>The good gods me presently,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.17>When I shall pray, 'O bless my lord and husband!'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.18>Undo that prayer, by crying out as loud,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.19>'O, bless my brother!' Husband win, win brother,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.20>Prays, and destroys the prayer; no midway</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.21>'Twixt these extremes at all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.4.22>Gentle Octavia,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.23>Let your best love draw to that point, which seeks</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.24>Best to preserve it: if I lose mine honour,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.25>I lose myself: better I were not yours</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.26>Than yours so branchless. But, as you requested,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.27>Yourself shall go between 's: the mean time, lady,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.28>I'll raise the preparation of a war</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.29>Shall stain your brother: make your soonest haste;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.30>So your desires are yours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.4.31>Thanks to my lord.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.32>The Jove of power make me most weak, most weak,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.33>Your reconciler! Wars 'twixt you twain would be</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.34>As if the world should cleave, and that slain men</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.35>Should solder up the rift.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.4.36>When it appears to you where this begins,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.37>Turn your displeasure that way: for our faults</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.38>Can never be so equal, that your love</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.39>Can equally move with them. Provide your going;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.40>Choose your own company, and command what cost</p>
<p class="line" name=3.4.41>Your heart has mind to.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE V. The same. Another room.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS and EROS, meeting</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.1>How now, friend Eros!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.2>There's strange news come, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.3>What, man?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.4>Caesar and Lepidus have made wars upon Pompey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.5>This is old: what is the success?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.6>Caesar, having made use of him in the wars 'gainst</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.7>Pompey, presently denied him rivality; would not let</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.8>him partake in the glory of the action: and not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.9>resting here, accuses him of letters he had formerly</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.10>wrote to Pompey; upon his own appeal, seizes him: so</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.11>the poor third is up, till death enlarge his confine.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.12>Then, world, thou hast a pair of chaps, no more;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.13>And throw between them all the food thou hast,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.14>They'll grind the one the other. Where's Antony?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.15>He's walking in the garden--thus; and spurns</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.16>The rush that lies before him; cries, 'Fool Lepidus!'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.17>And threats the throat of that his officer</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.18>That murder'd Pompey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.19>Our great navy's rigg'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.20>For Italy and Caesar. More, Domitius;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.21>My lord desires you presently: my news</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.22>I might have told hereafter.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.23>'Twill be naught:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.5.24>But let it be. Bring me to Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.5.25>Come, sir.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VI. Rome. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, AGRIPPA, and MECAENAS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.1>Contemning Rome, he has done all this, and more,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.2>In Alexandria: here's the manner of 't:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.3>I' the market-place, on a tribunal silver'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.4>Cleopatra and himself in chairs of gold</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.5>Were publicly enthroned: at the feet sat</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.6>Caesarion, whom they call my father's son,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.7>And all the unlawful issue that their lust</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.8>Since then hath made between them. Unto her</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.9>He gave the stablishment of Egypt; made her</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.10>Of lower Syria, Cyprus, Lydia,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.11>Absolute queen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.12>                  This in the public eye?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.13>I' the common show-place, where they exercise.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.14>His sons he there proclaim'd the kings of kings:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.15>Great Media, Parthia, and Armenia.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.16>He gave to Alexander; to Ptolemy he assign'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.17>Syria, Cilicia, and Phoenicia: she</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.18>In the habiliments of the goddess Isis</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.19>That day appear'd; and oft before gave audience,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.20>As 'tis reported, so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.21>Let Rome be thus Inform'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.22>Who, queasy with his insolence</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.23>Already, will their good thoughts call from him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.24>The people know it; and have now received</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.25>His accusations.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.26>                  Who does he accuse?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.27>Caesar: and that, having in Sicily</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.28>Sextus Pompeius spoil'd, we had not rated him</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.29>His part o' the isle: then does he say, he lent me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.30>Some shipping unrestored: lastly, he frets</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.31>That Lepidus of the triumvirate</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.32>Should be deposed; and, being, that we detain</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.33>All his revenue.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.34>                  Sir, this should be answer'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.35>'Tis done already, and the messenger gone.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.36>I have told him, Lepidus was grown too cruel;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.37>That he his high authority abused,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.38>And did deserve his change: for what I have conquer'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.39>I grant him part; but then, in his Armenia,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.40>And other of his conquer'd kingdoms, I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.41>Demand the like.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.42>                  He'll never yield to that.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.43>Nor must not then be yielded to in this.</p>
<p><i>Enter OCTAVIA with her train</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.44>Hail, Caesar, and my lord! hail, most dear Caesar!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.45>That ever I should call thee castaway!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.46>You have not call'd me so, nor have you cause.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.47>Why have you stol'n upon us thus! You come not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.48>Like Caesar's sister: the wife of Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.49>Should have an army for an usher, and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.50>The neighs of horse to tell of her approach</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.51>Long ere she did appear; the trees by the way</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.52>Should have borne men; and expectation fainted,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.53>Longing for what it had not; nay, the dust</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.54>Should have ascended to the roof of heaven,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.55>Raised by your populous troops: but you are come</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.56>A market-maid to Rome; and have prevented</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.57>The ostentation of our love, which, left unshown,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.58>Is often left unloved; we should have met you</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.59>By sea and land; supplying every stage</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.60>With an augmented greeting.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.61>Good my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.62>To come thus was I not constrain'd, but did</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.63>On my free will. My lord, Mark Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.64>Hearing that you prepared for war, acquainted</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.65>My grieved ear withal; whereon, I begg'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.66>His pardon for return.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.67>Which soon he granted,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.68>Being an obstruct 'tween his lust and him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.69>Do not say so, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.70>I have eyes upon him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.71>And his affairs come to me on the wind.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.72>Where is he now?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.73>                  My lord, in Athens.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.74>No, my most wronged sister; Cleopatra</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.75>Hath nodded him to her. He hath given his empire</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.76>Up to a whore; who now are levying</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.77>The kings o' the earth for war; he hath assembled</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.78>Bocchus, the king of Libya; Archelaus,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.79>Of Cappadocia; Philadelphos, king</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.80>Of Paphlagonia; the Thracian king, Adallas;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.81>King Malchus of Arabia; King of Pont;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.82>Herod of Jewry; Mithridates, king</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.83>Of Comagene; Polemon and Amyntas,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.84>The kings of Mede and Lycaonia,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.85>With a more larger list of sceptres.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.86>Ay me, most wretched,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.87>That have my heart parted betwixt two friends</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.88>That do afflict each other!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.89>Welcome hither:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.90>Your letters did withhold our breaking forth;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.91>Till we perceived, both how you were wrong led,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.92>And we in negligent danger. Cheer your heart;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.93>Be you not troubled with the time, which drives</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.94>O'er your content these strong necessities;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.95>But let determined things to destiny</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.96>Hold unbewail'd their way. Welcome to Rome;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.97>Nothing more dear to me. You are abused</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.98>Beyond the mark of thought: and the high gods,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.99>To do you justice, make them ministers</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.100>Of us and those that love you. Best of comfort;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.101>And ever welcome to us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.102>Welcome, lady.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.103>Welcome, dear madam.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.104>Each heart in Rome does love and pity you:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.105>Only the adulterous Antony, most large</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.106>In his abominations, turns you off;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.107>And gives his potent regiment to a trull,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.108>That noises it against us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>OCTAVIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.109>Is it so, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.6.110>Most certain. Sister, welcome: pray you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.6.111>Be ever known to patience: my dear'st sister!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VII. Near Actium. MARK ANTONY's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA and DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.1>I will be even with thee, doubt it not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.2>But why, why, why?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.3>Thou hast forspoke my being in these wars,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.4>And say'st it is not fit.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.5>Well, is it, is it?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.6>If not denounced against us, why should not we</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.7>Be there in person?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.8>[Aside]  Well, I could reply:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.9>If we should serve with horse and mares together,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.10>The horse were merely lost; the mares would bear</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.11>A soldier and his horse.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.12>What is't you say?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.13>Your presence needs must puzzle Antony;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.14>Take from his heart, take from his brain,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.15>from's time,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.16>What should not then be spared. He is already</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.17>Traduced for levity; and 'tis said in Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.18>That Photinus an eunuch and your maids</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.19>Manage this war.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.20>                  Sink Rome, and their tongues rot</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.21>That speak against us! A charge we bear i' the war,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.22>And, as the president of my kingdom, will</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.23>Appear there for a man. Speak not against it:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.24>I will not stay behind.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.25>Nay, I have done.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.26>Here comes the emperor.</p>
<p><i>Enter MARK ANTONY and CANIDIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.27>Is it not strange, Canidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.28>That from Tarentum and Brundusium</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.29>He could so quickly cut the Ionian sea,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.30>And take in Toryne? You have heard on't, sweet?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.31>Celerity is never more admired</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.32>Than by the negligent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.33>A good rebuke,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.34>Which might have well becomed the best of men,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.35>To taunt at slackness. Canidius, we</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.36>Will fight with him by sea.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.37>By sea! what else?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.38>Why will my lord do so?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.39>For that he dares us to't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.40>So hath my lord dared him to single fight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.41>Ay, and to wage this battle at Pharsalia.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.42>Where Caesar fought with Pompey: but these offers,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.43>Which serve not for his vantage, be shakes off;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.44>And so should you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.45>                  Your ships are not well mann'd;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.46>Your mariners are muleters, reapers, people</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.47>Ingross'd by swift impress; in Caesar's fleet</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.48>Are those that often have 'gainst Pompey fought:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.49>Their ships are yare; yours, heavy: no disgrace</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.50>Shall fall you for refusing him at sea,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.51>Being prepared for land.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.52>By sea, by sea.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.53>Most worthy sir, you therein throw away</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.54>The absolute soldiership you have by land;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.55>Distract your army, which doth most consist</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.56>Of war-mark'd footmen; leave unexecuted</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.57>Your own renowned knowledge; quite forego</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.58>The way which promises assurance; and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.59>Give up yourself merely to chance and hazard,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.60>From firm security.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.61>I'll fight at sea.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.62>I have sixty sails, Caesar none better.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.63>Our overplus of shipping will we burn;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.64>And, with the rest full-mann'd, from the head of Actium</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.65>Beat the approaching Caesar. But if we fail,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.66>We then can do't at land.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.67>Thy business?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.68>The news is true, my lord; he is descried;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.69>Caesar has taken Toryne.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.70>Can he be there in person? 'tis impossible;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.71>Strange that power should be. Canidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.72>Our nineteen legions thou shalt hold by land,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.73>And our twelve thousand horse. We'll to our ship:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.74>Away, my Thetis!</p>
<p><i>Enter a Soldier</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.75>How now, worthy soldier?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.76>O noble emperor, do not fight by sea;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.77>Trust not to rotten planks: do you misdoubt</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.78>This sword and these my wounds? Let the Egyptians</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.79>And the Phoenicians go a-ducking; we</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.80>Have used to conquer, standing on the earth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.81>And fighting foot to foot.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.82>Well, well: away!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt MARK ANTONY, QUEEN CLEOPATRA, and DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.83>By Hercules, I think I am i' the right.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.84>Soldier, thou art: but his whole action grows</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.85>Not in the power on't: so our leader's led,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.86>And we are women's men.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.87>You keep by land</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.88>The legions and the horse whole, do you not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.89>Marcus Octavius, Marcus Justeius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.90>Publicola, and Caelius, are for sea:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.91>But we keep whole by land. This speed of Caesar's</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.92>Carries beyond belief.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.93>While he was yet in Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.94>His power went out in such distractions as</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.95>Beguiled all spies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.96>Who's his lieutenant, hear you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.97>They say, one Taurus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.98>Well I know the man.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.99>The emperor calls Canidius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.7.100>With news the time's with labour, and throes forth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.7.101>Each minute, some.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VIII. A plain near Actium.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, and TAURUS, with his army, marching</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.8.1>Taurus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>TAURUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.8.2>My lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.8.3>Strike not by land; keep whole: provoke not battle,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.8.4>Till we have done at sea. Do not exceed</p>
<p class="line" name=3.8.5>The prescript of this scroll: our fortune lies</p>
<p class="line" name=3.8.6>Upon this jump.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IX. Another part of the plain.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY and DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.9.1>Set we our squadrons on yond side o' the hill,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.9.2>In eye of Caesar's battle; from which place</p>
<p class="line" name=3.9.3>We may the number of the ships behold,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.9.4>And so proceed accordingly.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE X. Another part of the plain.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>CANIDIUS marcheth with his land army one way over  the stage; and TAURUS, the lieutenant of OCTAVIUS  CAESAR, the other way. After their going in, is heard the noise of a sea-fight</i>
</blockquote>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Alarum. Enter DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.1>Naught, naught all, naught! I can behold no longer:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.2>The Antoniad, the Egyptian admiral,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.3>With all their sixty, fly and turn the rudder:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.4>To see't mine eyes are blasted.</p>
<p><i>Enter SCARUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.5>Gods and goddesses,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.6>All the whole synod of them!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.7>What's thy passion!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.8>The greater cantle of the world is lost</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.9>With very ignorance; we have kiss'd away</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.10>Kingdoms and provinces.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.11>How appears the fight?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.12>On our side like the token'd pestilence,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.13>Where death is sure. Yon ribaudred nag of Egypt,--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.14>Whom leprosy o'ertake!--i' the midst o' the fight,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.15>When vantage like a pair of twins appear'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.16>Both as the same, or rather ours the elder,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.17>The breese upon her, like a cow in June,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.18>Hoists sails and flies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.19>That I beheld:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.20>Mine eyes did sicken at the sight, and could not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.21>Endure a further view.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.22>She once being loof'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.23>The noble ruin of her magic, Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.24>Claps on his sea-wing, and, like a doting mallard,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.25>Leaving the fight in height, flies after her:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.26>I never saw an action of such shame;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.27>Experience, manhood, honour, ne'er before</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.28>Did violate so itself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.29>Alack, alack!</p>
<p><i>Enter CANIDIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.30>Our fortune on the sea is out of breath,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.31>And sinks most lamentably. Had our general</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.32>Been what he knew himself, it had gone well:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.33>O, he has given example for our flight,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.34>Most grossly, by his own!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.35>Ay, are you thereabouts?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.36>Why, then, good night indeed.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.37>Toward Peloponnesus are they fled.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.38>'Tis easy to't; and there I will attend</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.39>What further comes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CANIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.40>To Caesar will I render</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.41>My legions and my horse: six kings already</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.42>Show me the way of yielding.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.10.43>I'll yet follow</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.44>The wounded chance of Antony, though my reason</p>
<p class="line" name=3.10.45>Sits in the wind against me.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XI. Alexandria. CLEOPATRA's palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY with Attendants</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.1>Hark! the land bids me tread no more upon't;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.2>It is ashamed to bear me! Friends, come hither:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.3>I am so lated in the world, that I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.4>Have lost my way for ever: I have a ship</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.5>Laden with gold; take that, divide it; fly,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.6>And make your peace with Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.7>Fly! not we.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.8>I have fled myself; and have instructed cowards</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.9>To run and show their shoulders. Friends, be gone;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.10>I have myself resolved upon a course</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.11>Which has no need of you; be gone:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.12>My treasure's in the harbour, take it. O,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.13>I follow'd that I blush to look upon:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.14>My very hairs do mutiny; for the white</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.15>Reprove the brown for rashness, and they them</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.16>For fear and doting. Friends, be gone: you shall</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.17>Have letters from me to some friends that will</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.18>Sweep your way for you. Pray you, look not sad,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.19>Nor make replies of loathness: take the hint</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.20>Which my despair proclaims; let that be left</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.21>Which leaves itself: to the sea-side straightway:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.22>I will possess you of that ship and treasure.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.23>Leave me, I pray, a little: pray you now:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.24>Nay, do so; for, indeed, I have lost command,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.25>Therefore I pray you: I'll see you by and by.</p>
<p><i>Sits down</i></p>
<p><i>Enter CLEOPATRA led by CHARMIAN and IRAS; EROS following</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.26>Nay, gentle madam, to him, comfort him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.27>Do, most dear queen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.28>Do! why: what else?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.29>Let me sit down. O Juno!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.30>No, no, no, no, no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.31>See you here, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.32>O fie, fie, fie!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.33>Madam!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.34>Madam, O good empress!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.35>Sir, sir,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.36>Yes, my lord, yes; he at Philippi kept</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.37>His sword e'en like a dancer; while I struck</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.38>The lean and wrinkled Cassius; and 'twas I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.39>That the mad Brutus ended: he alone</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.40>Dealt on lieutenantry, and no practise had</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.41>In the brave squares of war: yet now--No matter.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.42>Ah, stand by.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.43>The queen, my lord, the queen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.44>Go to him, madam, speak to him:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.45>He is unqualitied with very shame.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.46>Well then, sustain him: O!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.47>Most noble sir, arise; the queen approaches:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.48>Her head's declined, and death will seize her, but</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.49>Your comfort makes the rescue.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.50>I have offended reputation,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.51>A most unnoble swerving.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.52>Sir, the queen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.53>O, whither hast thou led me, Egypt? See,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.54>How I convey my shame out of thine eyes</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.55>By looking back what I have left behind</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.56>'Stroy'd in dishonour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.57>O my lord, my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.58>Forgive my fearful sails! I little thought</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.59>You would have follow'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.60>Egypt, thou knew'st too well</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.61>My heart was to thy rudder tied by the strings,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.62>And thou shouldst tow me after: o'er my spirit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.63>Thy full supremacy thou knew'st, and that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.64>Thy beck might from the bidding of the gods</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.65>Command me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.66>          O, my pardon!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.67>Now I must</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.68>To the young man send humble treaties, dodge</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.69>And palter in the shifts of lowness; who</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.70>With half the bulk o' the world play'd as I pleased,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.71>Making and marring fortunes. You did know</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.72>How much you were my conqueror; and that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.73>My sword, made weak by my affection, would</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.74>Obey it on all cause.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.75>Pardon, pardon!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.11.76>Fall not a tear, I say; one of them rates</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.77>All that is won and lost: give me a kiss;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.78>Even this repays me. We sent our schoolmaster;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.79>Is he come back? Love, I am full of lead.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.80>Some wine, within there, and our viands! Fortune knows</p>
<p class="line" name=3.11.81>We scorn her most when most she offers blows.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XII. Egypt. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, DOLABELLA, THYREUS, with others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.1>Let him appear that's come from Antony.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.2>Know you him?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.3>                  Caesar, 'tis his schoolmaster:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.4>An argument that he is pluck'd, when hither</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.5>He sends so poor a pinion off his wing,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.6>Which had superfluous kings for messengers</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.7>Not many moons gone by.</p>
<p><i>Enter EUPHRONIUS, ambassador from MARK ANTONY</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.8>Approach, and speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>EUPHRONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.9>Such as I am, I come from Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.10>I was of late as petty to his ends</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.11>As is the morn-dew on the myrtle-leaf</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.12>To his grand sea.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.13>                  Be't so: declare thine office.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>EUPHRONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.14>Lord of his fortunes he salutes thee, and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.15>Requires to live in Egypt: which not granted,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.16>He lessens his requests; and to thee sues</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.17>To let him breathe between the heavens and earth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.18>A private man in Athens: this for him.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.19>Next, Cleopatra does confess thy greatness;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.20>Submits her to thy might; and of thee craves</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.21>The circle of the Ptolemies for her heirs,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.22>Now hazarded to thy grace.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.23>For Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.24>I have no ears to his request. The queen</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.25>Of audience nor desire shall fail, so she</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.26>From Egypt drive her all-disgraced friend,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.27>Or take his life there: this if she perform,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.28>She shall not sue unheard. So to them both.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>EUPHRONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.29>Fortune pursue thee!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.30>Bring him through the bands.</p>
<p><i>Exit EUPHRONIUS</i></p>
<p><i>To THYREUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.31>From Antony win Cleopatra: promise,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.32>And in our name, what she requires; add more,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.33>From thine invention, offers: women are not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.34>In their best fortunes strong; but want will perjure</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.35>The ne'er touch'd vestal: try thy cunning, Thyreus;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.36>Make thine own edict for thy pains, which we</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.37>Will answer as a law.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.38>Caesar, I go.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.39>Observe how Antony becomes his flaw,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.40>And what thou think'st his very action speaks</p>
<p class="line" name=3.12.41>In every power that moves.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.12.42>Caesar, I shall.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XIII. Alexandria. CLEOPATRA's palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA, DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS, CHARMIAN, and IRAS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.1>What shall we do, Enobarbus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.2>Think, and die.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.3>Is Antony or we in fault for this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.4>Antony only, that would make his will</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.5>Lord of his reason. What though you fled</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.6>From that great face of war, whose several ranges</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.7>Frighted each other? why should he follow?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.8>The itch of his affection should not then</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.9>Have nick'd his captainship; at such a point,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.10>When half to half the world opposed, he being</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.11>The meered question: 'twas a shame no less</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.12>Than was his loss, to course your flying flags,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.13>And leave his navy gazing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.14>Prithee, peace.</p>
<p><i>Enter MARK ANTONY with EUPHRONIUS, the Ambassador</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.15>Is that his answer?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>EUPHRONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.16>Ay, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.17>The queen shall then have courtesy, so she</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.18>Will yield us up.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>EUPHRONIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.19>                  He says so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.20>Let her know't.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.21>To the boy Caesar send this grizzled head,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.22>And he will fill thy wishes to the brim</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.23>With principalities.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.24>That head, my lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.25>To him again: tell him he wears the rose</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.26>Of youth upon him; from which the world should note</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.27>Something particular: his coin, ships, legions,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.28>May be a coward's; whose ministers would prevail</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.29>Under the service of a child as soon</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.30>As i' the command of Caesar: I dare him therefore</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.31>To lay his gay comparisons apart,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.32>And answer me declined, sword against sword,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.33>Ourselves alone. I'll write it: follow me.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt MARK ANTONY and EUPHRONIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.34>[Aside]  Yes, like enough, high-battled Caesar will</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.35>Unstate his happiness, and be staged to the show,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.36>Against a sworder! I see men's judgments are</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.37>A parcel of their fortunes; and things outward</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.38>Do draw the inward quality after them,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.39>To suffer all alike. That he should dream,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.40>Knowing all measures, the full Caesar will</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.41>Answer his emptiness! Caesar, thou hast subdued</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.42>His judgment too.</p>
<p><i>Enter an Attendant</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Attendant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.43>                  A messenger from CAESAR.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.44>What, no more ceremony? See, my women!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.45>Against the blown rose may they stop their nose</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.46>That kneel'd unto the buds. Admit him, sir.</p>
<p><i>Exit Attendant</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.47>[Aside]  Mine honesty and I begin to square.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.48>The loyalty well held to fools does make</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.49>Our faith mere folly: yet he that can endure</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.50>To follow with allegiance a fall'n lord</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.51>Does conquer him that did his master conquer</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.52>And earns a place i' the story.</p>
<p><i>Enter THYREUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.53>Caesar's will?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.54>Hear it apart.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.55>                  None but friends: say boldly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.56>So, haply, are they friends to Antony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.57>He needs as many, sir, as Caesar has;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.58>Or needs not us. If Caesar please, our master</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.59>Will leap to be his friend: for us, you know,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.60>Whose he is we are, and that is, Caesar's.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.61>So.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.62>Thus then, thou most renown'd: Caesar entreats,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.63>Not to consider in what case thou stand'st,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.64>Further than he is Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.65>Go on: right royal.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.66>He knows that you embrace not Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.67>As you did love, but as you fear'd him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.68>O!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.69>The scars upon your honour, therefore, he</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.70>Does pity, as constrained blemishes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.71>Not as deserved.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.72>                  He is a god, and knows</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.73>What is most right: mine honour was not yielded,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.74>But conquer'd merely.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.75>[Aside]             To be sure of that,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.76>I will ask Antony. Sir, sir, thou art so leaky,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.77>That we must leave thee to thy sinking, for</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.78>Thy dearest quit thee.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.79>Shall I say to Caesar</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.80>What you require of him? for he partly begs</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.81>To be desired to give. It much would please him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.82>That of his fortunes you should make a staff</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.83>To lean upon: but it would warm his spirits,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.84>To hear from me you had left Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.85>And put yourself under his shrowd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.86>The universal landlord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.87>What's your name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.88>My name is Thyreus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.89>Most kind messenger,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.90>Say to great Caesar this: in deputation</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.91>I kiss his conquering hand: tell him, I am prompt</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.92>To lay my crown at 's feet, and there to kneel:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.93>Tell him from his all-obeying breath I hear</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.94>The doom of Egypt.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.95>'Tis your noblest course.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.96>Wisdom and fortune combating together,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.97>If that the former dare but what it can,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.98>No chance may shake it. Give me grace to lay</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.99>My duty on your hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.100>Your Caesar's father oft,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.101>When he hath mused of taking kingdoms in,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.102>Bestow'd his lips on that unworthy place,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.103>As it rain'd kisses.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter MARK ANTONY and DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.104>Favours, by Jove that thunders!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.105>What art thou, fellow?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.106>One that but performs</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.107>The bidding of the fullest man, and worthiest</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.108>To have command obey'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.109>[Aside]               You will be whipp'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.110>Approach, there! Ah, you kite! Now, gods</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.111>and devils!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.112>Authority melts from me: of late, when I cried 'Ho!'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.113>Like boys unto a muss, kings would start forth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.114>And cry 'Your will?' Have you no ears? I am</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.115>Antony yet.</p>
<p><i>Enter Attendants</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.116>Take hence this Jack, and whip him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.117>[Aside]  'Tis better playing with a lion's whelp</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.118>Than with an old one dying.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.119>Moon and stars!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.120>Whip him. Were't twenty of the greatest tributaries</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.121>That do acknowledge Caesar, should I find them</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.122>So saucy with the hand of she here,--what's her name,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.123>Since she was Cleopatra? Whip him, fellows,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.124>Till, like a boy, you see him cringe his face,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.125>And whine aloud for mercy: take him hence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>THYREUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.126>Mark Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.127>                  Tug him away: being whipp'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.128>Bring him again: this Jack of Caesar's shall</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.129>Bear us an errand to him.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Attendants with THYREUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.130>You were half blasted ere I knew you: ha!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.131>Have I my pillow left unpress'd in Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.132>Forborne the getting of a lawful race,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.133>And by a gem of women, to be abused</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.134>By one that looks on feeders?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.135>Good my lord,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.136>You have been a boggler ever:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.137>But when we in our viciousness grow hard--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.138>O misery on't!--the wise gods seel our eyes;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.139>In our own filth drop our clear judgments; make us</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.140>Adore our errors; laugh at's, while we strut</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.141>To our confusion.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.142>                  O, is't come to this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.143>I found you as a morsel cold upon</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.144>Dead Caesar's trencher; nay, you were a fragment</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.145>Of Cneius Pompey's; besides what hotter hours,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.146>Unregister'd in vulgar fame, you have</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.147>Luxuriously pick'd out: for, I am sure,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.148>Though you can guess what temperance should be,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.149>You know not what it is.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.150>Wherefore is this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.151>To let a fellow that will take rewards</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.152>And say 'God quit you!' be familiar with</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.153>My playfellow, your hand; this kingly seal</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.154>And plighter of high hearts! O, that I were</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.155>Upon the hill of Basan, to outroar</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.156>The horned herd! for I have savage cause;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.157>And to proclaim it civilly, were like</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.158>A halter'd neck which does the hangman thank</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.159>For being yare about him.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter Attendants with THYREUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.160>Is he whipp'd?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>First Attendant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.161>Soundly, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.162>                  Cried he? and begg'd a' pardon?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>First Attendant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.163>He did ask favour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.164>If that thy father live, let him repent</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.165>Thou wast not made his daughter; and be thou sorry</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.166>To follow Caesar in his triumph, since</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.167>Thou hast been whipp'd for following him: henceforth</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.168>The white hand of a lady fever thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.169>Shake thou to look on 't. Get thee back to Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.170>Tell him thy entertainment: look, thou say</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.171>He makes me angry with him; for he seems</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.172>Proud and disdainful, harping on what I am,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.173>Not what he knew I was: he makes me angry;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.174>And at this time most easy 'tis to do't,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.175>When my good stars, that were my former guides,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.176>Have empty left their orbs, and shot their fires</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.177>Into the abysm of hell. If he mislike</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.178>My speech and what is done, tell him he has</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.179>Hipparchus, my enfranched bondman, whom</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.180>He may at pleasure whip, or hang, or torture,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.181>As he shall like, to quit me: urge it thou:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.182>Hence with thy stripes, begone!</p>
<p><i>Exit THYREUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.183>Have you done yet?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.184>                  Alack, our terrene moon</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.185>Is now eclipsed; and it portends alone</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.186>The fall of Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.187>I must stay his time.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.188>To flatter Caesar, would you mingle eyes</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.189>With one that ties his points?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.190>Not know me yet?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.191>Cold-hearted toward me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.192>Ah, dear, if I be so,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.193>From my cold heart let heaven engender hail,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.194>And poison it in the source; and the first stone</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.195>Drop in my neck: as it determines, so</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.196>Dissolve my life! The next Caesarion smite!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.197>Till by degrees the memory of my womb,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.198>Together with my brave Egyptians all,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.199>By the discandying of this pelleted storm,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.200>Lie graveless, till the flies and gnats of Nile</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.201>Have buried them for prey!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.202>I am satisfied.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.203>Caesar sits down in Alexandria; where</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.204>I will oppose his fate. Our force by land</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.205>Hath nobly held; our sever'd navy too</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.206>Have knit again, and fleet, threatening most sea-like.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.207>Where hast thou been, my heart? Dost thou hear, lady?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.208>If from the field I shall return once more</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.209>To kiss these lips, I will appear in blood;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.210>I and my sword will earn our chronicle:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.211>There's hope in't yet.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.212>That's my brave lord!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.213>I will be treble-sinew'd, hearted, breathed,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.214>And fight maliciously: for when mine hours</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.215>Were nice and lucky, men did ransom lives</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.216>Of me for jests; but now I'll set my teeth,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.217>And send to darkness all that stop me. Come,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.218>Let's have one other gaudy night: call to me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.219>All my sad captains; fill our bowls once more;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.220>Let's mock the midnight bell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.221>It is my birth-day:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.222>I had thought to have held it poor: but, since my lord</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.223>Is Antony again, I will be Cleopatra.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.224>We will yet do well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.225>Call all his noble captains to my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.226>Do so, we'll speak to them; and to-night I'll force</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.227>The wine peep through their scars. Come on, my queen;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.228>There's sap in't yet. The next time I do fight,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.229>I'll make death love me; for I will contend</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.230>Even with his pestilent scythe.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.13.231>Now he'll outstare the lightning. To be furious,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.232>Is to be frighted out of fear; and in that mood</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.233>The dove will peck the estridge; and I see still,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.234>A diminution in our captain's brain</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.235>Restores his heart: when valour preys on reason,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.236>It eats the sword it fights with. I will seek</p>
<p class="line" name=3.13.237>Some way to leave him.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT IV</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Before Alexandria. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, AGRIPPA, and MECAENAS, with his Army; OCTAVIUS CAESAR reading a letter</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.1>He calls me boy; and chides, as he had power</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.2>To beat me out of Egypt; my messenger</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.3>He hath whipp'd with rods; dares me to personal combat,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.4>Caesar to Antony: let the old ruffian know</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.5>I have many other ways to die; meantime</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.6>Laugh at his challenge.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.7>Caesar must think,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.8>When one so great begins to rage, he's hunted</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.9>Even to falling. Give him no breath, but now</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.10>Make boot of his distraction: never anger</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.11>Made good guard for itself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.12>Let our best heads</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.13>Know, that to-morrow the last of many battles</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.14>We mean to fight: within our files there are,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.15>Of those that served Mark Antony but late,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.16>Enough to fetch him in. See it done:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.17>And feast the army; we have store to do't,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.18>And they have earn'd the waste. Poor Antony!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. Alexandria. CLEOPATRA's palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY, CLEOPATRA, DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS, CHARMIAN, IRAS, ALEXAS, with others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.1>He will not fight with me, Domitius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.2>No.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.3>Why should he not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.4>He thinks, being twenty times of better fortune,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.5>He is twenty men to one.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.6>To-morrow, soldier,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.7>By sea and land I'll fight: or I will live,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.8>Or bathe my dying honour in the blood</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.9>Shall make it live again. Woo't thou fight well?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.10>I'll strike, and cry 'Take all.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.11>Well said; come on.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.12>Call forth my household servants: let's to-night</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.13>Be bounteous at our meal.</p>
<p><i>Enter three or four Servitors</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.14>Give me thy hand,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.15>Thou hast been rightly honest;--so hast thou;--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.16>Thou,--and thou,--and thou:--you have served me well,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.17>And kings have been your fellows.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.18>[Aside to DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS]  What means this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.19>[Aside to CLEOPATRA]  'Tis one of those odd</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.20>tricks which sorrow shoots</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.21>Out of the mind.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.22>                  And thou art honest too.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.23>I wish I could be made so many men,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.24>And all of you clapp'd up together in</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.25>An Antony, that I might do you service</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.26>So good as you have done.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.27>The gods forbid!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.28>Well, my good fellows, wait on me to-night:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.29>Scant not my cups; and make as much of me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.30>As when mine empire was your fellow too,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.31>And suffer'd my command.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.32>[Aside to DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS]  What does he mean?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.33>[Aside to CLEOPATRA]  To make his followers weep.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.34>Tend me to-night;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.35>May be it is the period of your duty:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.36>Haply you shall not see me more; or if,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.37>A mangled shadow: perchance to-morrow</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.38>You'll serve another master. I look on you</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.39>As one that takes his leave. Mine honest friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.40>I turn you not away; but, like a master</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.41>Married to your good service, stay till death:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.42>Tend me to-night two hours, I ask no more,</p>
