<p class="line" name=4.2.43>And the gods yield you for't!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.44>What mean you, sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.45>To give them this discomfort? Look, they weep;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.46>And I, an ass, am onion-eyed: for shame,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.47>Transform us not to women.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.48>Ho, ho, ho!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.49>Now the witch take me, if I meant it thus!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.50>Grace grow where those drops fall!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.51>My hearty friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.52>You take me in too dolorous a sense;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.53>For I spake to you for your comfort; did desire you</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.54>To burn this night with torches: know, my hearts,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.55>I hope well of to-morrow; and will lead you</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.56>Where rather I'll expect victorious life</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.57>Than death and honour. Let's to supper, come,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.58>And drown consideration.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. The same. Before the palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter two Soldiers to their guard</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.1>Brother, good night: to-morrow is the day.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.2>It will determine one way: fare you well.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.3>Heard you of nothing strange about the streets?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.4>Nothing. What news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.5>Belike 'tis but a rumour. Good night to you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.6>Well, sir, good night.</p>
<p><i>Enter two other Soldiers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.7>Soldiers, have careful watch.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.8>And you. Good night, good night.</p>
<p><i>They place themselves in every corner of the stage</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Fourth Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.9>Here we: and if to-morrow</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.10>Our navy thrive, I have an absolute hope</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.11>Our landmen will stand up.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.12>'Tis a brave army,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.13>And full of purpose.</p>
<p><i>Music of the hautboys as under the stage</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Fourth Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.14>Peace! what noise?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.15>List, list!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.16>Hark!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.17>    Music i' the air.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.18>Under the earth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Fourth Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.19>It signs well, does it not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.20>No.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.21>Peace, I say!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.22>What should this mean?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.23>'Tis the god Hercules, whom Antony loved,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.24>Now leaves him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.25>Walk; let's see if other watchmen</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.26>Do hear what we do?</p>
<p><i>They advance to another post</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.27>How now, masters!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.28>[Speaking together]  How now!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.29>How now! do you hear this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.30>Ay; is't not strange?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.31>Do you hear, masters? do you hear?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.32>Follow the noise so far as we have quarter;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.33>Let's see how it will give off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.34>Content. 'Tis strange.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. The same. A room in the palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY and CLEOPATRA, CHARMIAN, and others attending</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.1>Eros! mine armour, Eros!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.2>Sleep a little.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.3>No, my chuck. Eros, come; mine armour, Eros!</p>
<p><i>Enter EROS with armour</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.4>Come good fellow, put mine iron on:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.5>If fortune be not ours to-day, it is</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.6>Because we brave her: come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.7>Nay, I'll help too.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.8>What's this for?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.9>                  Ah, let be, let be! thou art</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.10>The armourer of my heart: false, false; this, this.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.11>Sooth, la, I'll help: thus it must be.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.12>Well, well;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.13>We shall thrive now. Seest thou, my good fellow?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.14>Go put on thy defences.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.15>Briefly, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.16>Is not this buckled well?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.17>Rarely, rarely:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.18>He that unbuckles this, till we do please</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.19>To daff't for our repose, shall hear a storm.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.20>Thou fumblest, Eros; and my queen's a squire</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.21>More tight at this than thou: dispatch. O love,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.22>That thou couldst see my wars to-day, and knew'st</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.23>The royal occupation! thou shouldst see</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.24>A workman in't.</p>
<p><i>Enter an armed Soldier</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.25>Good morrow to thee; welcome:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.26>Thou look'st like him that knows a warlike charge:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.27>To business that we love we rise betime,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.28>And go to't with delight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.29>A thousand, sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.30>Early though't be, have on their riveted trim,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.31>And at the port expect you.</p>
<p><i>Shout. Trumpets flourish</i></p>
<p><i>Enter Captains and Soldiers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Captain</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.32>The morn is fair. Good morrow, general.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.33>Good morrow, general.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.34>'Tis well blown, lads:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.35>This morning, like the spirit of a youth</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.36>That means to be of note, begins betimes.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.37>So, so; come, give me that: this way; well said.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.38>Fare thee well, dame, whate'er becomes of me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.39>This is a soldier's kiss: rebukeable</p>
<p><i>Kisses her</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.40>And worthy shameful cheque it were, to stand</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.41>On more mechanic compliment; I'll leave thee</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.42>Now, like a man of steel. You that will fight,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.43>Follow me close; I'll bring you to't. Adieu.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt MARK ANTONY, EROS, Captains, and Soldiers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.44>Please you, retire to your chamber.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.45>Lead me.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.46>He goes forth gallantly. That he and Caesar might</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.47>Determine this great war in single fight!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.48>Then Antony,--but now--Well, on.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE V. Alexandria. MARK ANTONY's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Trumpets sound. Enter MARK ANTONY and EROS; a Soldier meeting them</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.1>The gods make this a happy day to Antony!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.2>Would thou and those thy scars had once prevail'd</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.3>To make me fight at land!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.4>Hadst thou done so,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.5>The kings that have revolted, and the soldier</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.6>That has this morning left thee, would have still</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.7>Follow'd thy heels.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.8>Who's gone this morning?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.9>Who!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.10>One ever near thee: call for Enobarbus,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.11>He shall not hear thee; or from Caesar's camp</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.12>Say 'I am none of thine.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.13>What say'st thou?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.14>Sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.15>He is with Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.16>                  Sir, his chests and treasure</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.17>He has not with him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.18>Is he gone?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.19>Most certain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.20>Go, Eros, send his treasure after; do it;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.21>Detain no jot, I charge thee: write to him--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.22>I will subscribe--gentle adieus and greetings;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.23>Say that I wish he never find more cause</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.24>To change a master. O, my fortunes have</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.25>Corrupted honest men! Dispatch.--Enobarbus!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VI. Alexandria. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Flourish. Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, AGRIPPA, with DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS, and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.1>Go forth, Agrippa, and begin the fight:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.2>Our will is Antony be took alive;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.3>Make it so known.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.4>Caesar, I shall.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.5>The time of universal peace is near:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.6>Prove this a prosperous day, the three-nook'd world</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.7>Shall bear the olive freely.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.8>Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.9>Is come into the field.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.10>Go charge Agrippa</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.11>Plant those that have revolted in the van,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.12>That Antony may seem to spend his fury</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.13>Upon himself.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.14>Alexas did revolt; and went to Jewry on</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.15>Affairs of Antony; there did persuade</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.16>Great Herod to incline himself to Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.17>And leave his master Antony: for this pains</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.18>Caesar hath hang'd him. Canidius and the rest</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.19>That fell away have entertainment, but</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.20>No honourable trust. I have done ill;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.21>Of which I do accuse myself so sorely,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.22>That I will joy no more.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Soldier of CAESAR's</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.23>Enobarbus, Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.24>Hath after thee sent all thy treasure, with</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.25>His bounty overplus: the messenger</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.26>Came on my guard; and at thy tent is now</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.27>Unloading of his mules.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.28>I give it you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.29>Mock not, Enobarbus.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.30>I tell you true: best you safed the bringer</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.31>Out of the host; I must attend mine office,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.32>Or would have done't myself. Your emperor</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.33>Continues still a Jove.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.34>I am alone the villain of the earth,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.35>And feel I am so most. O Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.36>Thou mine of bounty, how wouldst thou have paid</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.37>My better service, when my turpitude</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.38>Thou dost so crown with gold! This blows my heart:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.39>If swift thought break it not, a swifter mean</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.40>Shall outstrike thought: but thought will do't, I feel.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.41>I fight against thee! No: I will go seek</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.42>Some ditch wherein to die; the foul'st best fits</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.43>My latter part of life.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VII. Field of battle between the camps.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Alarum. Drums and trumpets. Enter AGRIPPA and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.1>Retire, we have engaged ourselves too far:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.2>Caesar himself has work, and our oppression</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.3>Exceeds what we expected.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<p><i>Alarums. Enter MARK ANTONY and SCARUS wounded</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.4>O my brave emperor, this is fought indeed!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.5>Had we done so at first, we had droven them home</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.6>With clouts about their heads.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.7>Thou bleed'st apace.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.8>I had a wound here that was like a T,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.9>But now 'tis made an H.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.10>They do retire.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.11>We'll beat 'em into bench-holes: I have yet</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.12>Room for six scotches more.</p>
<p><i>Enter EROS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.13>They are beaten, sir, and our advantage serves</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.14>For a fair victory.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.15>Let us score their backs,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.16>And snatch 'em up, as we take hares, behind:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.17>'Tis sport to maul a runner.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.18>I will reward thee</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.19>Once for thy spritely comfort, and ten-fold</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.20>For thy good valour. Come thee on.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.21>I'll halt after.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VIII. Under the walls of Alexandria.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Alarum. Enter MARK ANTONY, in a march; SCARUS, with others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.8.1>We have beat him to his camp: run one before,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.2>And let the queen know of our gests. To-morrow,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.3>Before the sun shall see 's, we'll spill the blood</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.4>That has to-day escaped. I thank you all;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.5>For doughty-handed are you, and have fought</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.6>Not as you served the cause, but as 't had been</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.7>Each man's like mine; you have shown all Hectors.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.8>Enter the city, clip your wives, your friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.9>Tell them your feats; whilst they with joyful tears</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.10>Wash the congealment from your wounds, and kiss</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.11>The honour'd gashes whole.</p>
<p><i>To SCARUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.12>Give me thy hand</p>
<p><i>Enter CLEOPATRA, attended</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.13>To this great fairy I'll commend thy acts,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.14>Make her thanks bless thee.</p>
<p><i>To CLEOPATRA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.15>O thou day o' the world,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.16>Chain mine arm'd neck; leap thou, attire and all,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.17>Through proof of harness to my heart, and there</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.18>Ride on the pants triumphing!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.8.19>Lord of lords!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.20>O infinite virtue, comest thou smiling from</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.21>The world's great snare uncaught?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.8.22>My nightingale,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.23>We have beat them to their beds. What, girl!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.24>though grey</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.25>Do something mingle with our younger brown, yet ha' we</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.26>A brain that nourishes our nerves, and can</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.27>Get goal for goal of youth. Behold this man;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.28>Commend unto his lips thy favouring hand:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.29>Kiss it, my warrior: he hath fought to-day</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.30>As if a god, in hate of mankind, had</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.31>Destroy'd in such a shape.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.8.32>I'll give thee, friend,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.33>An armour all of gold; it was a king's.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.8.34>He has deserved it, were it carbuncled</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.35>Like holy Phoebus' car. Give me thy hand:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.36>Through Alexandria make a jolly march;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.37>Bear our hack'd targets like the men that owe them:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.38>Had our great palace the capacity</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.39>To camp this host, we all would sup together,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.40>And drink carouses to the next day's fate,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.41>Which promises royal peril. Trumpeters,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.42>With brazen din blast you the city's ear;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.43>Make mingle with rattling tabourines;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.44>That heaven and earth may strike their sounds together,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.8.45>Applauding our approach.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IX. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Sentinels at their post</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.1>If we be not relieved within this hour,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.2>We must return to the court of guard: the night</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.3>Is shiny; and they say we shall embattle</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.4>By the second hour i' the morn.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.5>This last day was</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.6>A shrewd one to's.</p>
<p><i>Enter DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.7>                  O, bear me witness, night,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.8>What man is this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.9>                  Stand close, and list him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.10>Be witness to me, O thou blessed moon,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.11>When men revolted shall upon record</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.12>Bear hateful memory, poor Enobarbus did</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.13>Before thy face repent!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.14>Enobarbus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.15>Peace!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.16>Hark further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>DOMITIUS ENOBARBUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.17>O sovereign mistress of true melancholy,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.18>The poisonous damp of night disponge upon me,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.19>That life, a very rebel to my will,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.20>May hang no longer on me: throw my heart</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.21>Against the flint and hardness of my fault:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.22>Which, being dried with grief, will break to powder,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.23>And finish all foul thoughts. O Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.24>Nobler than my revolt is infamous,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.25>Forgive me in thine own particular;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.26>But let the world rank me in register</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.27>A master-leaver and a fugitive:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.28>O Antony! O Antony!</p>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.29>Let's speak To him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.30>Let's hear him, for the things he speaks</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.31>May concern Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.32>Let's do so. But he sleeps.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.33>Swoons rather; for so bad a prayer as his</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.34>Was never yet for sleep.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.35>Go we to him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.36>Awake, sir, awake; speak to us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Second Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.37>Hear you, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.38>The hand of death hath raught him.</p>
<p><i>Drums afar off</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.39>Hark! the drums</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.40>Demurely wake the sleepers. Let us bear him</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.41>To the court of guard; he is of note: our hour</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.42>Is fully out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Third Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.9.43>Come on, then;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.9.44>He may recover yet.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt with the body</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE X. Between the two camps.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY and SCARUS, with their Army</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.10.1>Their preparation is to-day by sea;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.2>We please them not by land.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.10.3>For both, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.10.4>I would they'ld fight i' the fire or i' the air;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.5>We'ld fight there too. But this it is; our foot</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.6>Upon the hills adjoining to the city</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.7>Shall stay with us: order for sea is given;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.8>They have put forth the haven</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.9>Where their appointment we may best discover,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.10.10>And look on their endeavour.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XI. Another part of the same.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, and his Army</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.11.1>But being charged, we will be still by land,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.11.2>Which, as I take't, we shall; for his best force</p>
<p class="line" name=4.11.3>Is forth to man his galleys. To the vales,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.11.4>And hold our best advantage.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XII. Another part of the same.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY and SCARUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.12.1>Yet they are not join'd: where yond pine</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.2>does stand,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.3>I shall discover all: I'll bring thee word</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.4>Straight, how 'tis like to go.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>SCARUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.12.5>Swallows have built</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.6>In Cleopatra's sails their nests: the augurers</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.7>Say they know not, they cannot tell; look grimly,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.8>And dare not speak their knowledge. Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.9>Is valiant, and dejected; and, by starts,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.10>His fretted fortunes give him hope, and fear,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.11>Of what he has, and has not.</p>
<p><i>Alarum afar off, as at a sea-fight</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter MARK ANTONY</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.12.12>All is lost;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.13>This foul Egyptian hath betrayed me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.14>My fleet hath yielded to the foe; and yonder</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.15>They cast their caps up and carouse together</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.16>Like friends long lost. Triple-turn'd whore!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.17>'tis thou</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.18>Hast sold me to this novice; and my heart</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.19>Makes only wars on thee. Bid them all fly;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.20>For when I am revenged upon my charm,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.21>I have done all. Bid them all fly; begone.</p>
<p><i>Exit SCARUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.22>O sun, thy uprise shall I see no more:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.23>Fortune and Antony part here; even here</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.24>Do we shake hands. All come to this? The hearts</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.25>That spaniel'd me at heels, to whom I gave</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.26>Their wishes, do discandy, melt their sweets</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.27>On blossoming Caesar; and this pine is bark'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.28>That overtopp'd them all. Betray'd I am:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.29>O this false soul of Egypt! this grave charm,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.30>Whose eye beck'd forth my wars, and call'd them home;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.31>Whose bosom was my crownet, my chief end,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.32>Like a right gipsy, hath, at fast and loose,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.33>Beguiled me to the very heart of loss.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.34>What, Eros, Eros!</p>
<p><i>Enter CLEOPATRA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.35>Ah, thou spell! Avaunt!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.12.36>Why is my lord enraged against his love?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.12.37>Vanish, or I shall give thee thy deserving,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.38>And blemish Caesar's triumph. Let him take thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.39>And hoist thee up to the shouting plebeians:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.40>Follow his chariot, like the greatest spot</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.41>Of all thy sex; most monster-like, be shown</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.42>For poor'st diminutives, for doits; and let</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.43>Patient Octavia plough thy visage up</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.44>With her prepared nails.</p>
<p><i>Exit CLEOPATRA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.45>'Tis well thou'rt gone,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.46>If it be well to live; but better 'twere</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.47>Thou fell'st into my fury, for one death</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.48>Might have prevented many. Eros, ho!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.49>The shirt of Nessus is upon me: teach me,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.50>Alcides, thou mine ancestor, thy rage:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.51>Let me lodge Lichas on the horns o' the moon;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.52>And with those hands, that grasp'd the heaviest club,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.53>Subdue my worthiest self. The witch shall die:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.54>To the young Roman boy she hath sold me, and I fall</p>
<p class="line" name=4.12.55>Under this plot; she dies for't. Eros, ho!</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XIII. Alexandria. Cleopatra's palace.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA, CHARMIAN, IRAS, and MARDIAN</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.13.1>Help me, my women! O, he is more mad</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.2>Than Telamon for his shield; the boar of Thessaly</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.3>Was never so emboss'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.13.4>To the monument!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.5>There lock yourself, and send him word you are dead.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.6>The soul and body rive not more in parting</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.7>Than greatness going off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.13.8>To the monument!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.9>Mardian, go tell him I have slain myself;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.10>Say, that the last I spoke was 'Antony,'</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.11>And word it, prithee, piteously: hence, Mardian,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.12>And bring me how he takes my death.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.13.13>To the monument!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XIV. The same. Another room.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MARK ANTONY and EROS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.1>Eros, thou yet behold'st me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.2>Ay, noble lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.3>Sometimes we see a cloud that's dragonish;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.4>A vapour sometime like a bear or lion,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.5>A tower'd citadel, a pendent rock,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.6>A forked mountain, or blue promontory</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.7>With trees upon't, that nod unto the world,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.8>And mock our eyes with air: thou hast seen</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.9>these signs;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.10>They are black vesper's pageants.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.11>Ay, my lord,</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.12>That which is now a horse, even with a thought</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.13>The rack dislimns, and makes it indistinct,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.14>As water is in water.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.15>It does, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.16>My good knave Eros, now thy captain is</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.17>Even such a body: here I am Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.18>Yet cannot hold this visible shape, my knave.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.19>I made these wars for Egypt: and the queen,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.20>Whose heart I thought I had, for she had mine;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.21>Which whilst it was mine had annex'd unto't</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.22>A million more, now lost,--she, Eros, has</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.23>Pack'd cards with Caesar, and false-play'd my glory</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.24>Unto an enemy's triumph.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.25>Nay, weep not, gentle Eros; there is left us</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.26>Ourselves to end ourselves.</p>
<p><i>Enter MARDIAN</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.27>O! thy vile lady!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.28>She has robb'd me of my sword.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MARDIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.29>No, Antony;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.30>My mistress loved thee, and her fortunes mingled</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.31>With thine entirely.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.32>Hence, saucy eunuch; peace!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.33>She hath betray'd me and shall die the death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARDIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.34>Death of one person can be paid but once,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.35>And that she has discharged: what thou wouldst do</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.36>Is done unto thy hand: the last she spake</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.37>Was 'Antony! most noble Antony!'</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.38>Then in the midst a tearing groan did break</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.39>The name of Antony; it was divided</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.40>Between her heart and lips: she render'd life,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.41>Thy name so buried in her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.42>Dead, then?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MARDIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.43>Dead.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.44>Unarm, Eros; the long day's task is done,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.45>And we must sleep.</p>
<p><i>To MARDIAN</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.46>That thou depart'st hence safe,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.47>Does pay thy labour richly; go.</p>
<p><i>Exit MARDIAN</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.48>Off, pluck off:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.49>The seven-fold shield of Ajax cannot keep</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.50>The battery from my heart. O, cleave, my sides!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.51>Heart, once be stronger than thy continent,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.52>Crack thy frail case! Apace, Eros, apace.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.53>No more a soldier: bruised pieces, go;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.54>You have been nobly borne. From me awhile.</p>
<p><i>Exit EROS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.55>I will o'ertake thee, Cleopatra, and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.56>Weep for my pardon. So it must be, for now</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.57>All length is torture: since the torch is out,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.58>Lie down, and stray no farther: now all labour</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.59>Mars what it does; yea, very force entangles</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.60>Itself with strength: seal then, and all is done.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.61>Eros!--I come, my queen:--Eros!--Stay for me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.62>Where souls do couch on flowers, we'll hand in hand,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.63>And with our sprightly port make the ghosts gaze:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.64>Dido and her AEneas shall want troops,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.65>And all the haunt be ours. Come, Eros, Eros!</p>
<p><i>Re-enter EROS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.66>What would my lord?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.67>Since Cleopatra died,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.68>I have lived in such dishonour, that the gods</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.69>Detest my baseness. I, that with my sword</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.70>Quarter'd the world, and o'er green Neptune's back</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.71>With ships made cities, condemn myself to lack</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.72>The courage of a woman; less noble mind</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.73>Than she which by her death our Caesar tells</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.74>'I am conqueror of myself.' Thou art sworn, Eros,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.75>That, when the exigent should come, which now</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.76>Is come indeed, when I should see behind me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.77>The inevitable prosecution of</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.78>Disgrace and horror, that, on my command,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.79>Thou then wouldst kill me: do't; the time is come:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.80>Thou strikest not me, 'tis Caesar thou defeat'st.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.81>Put colour in thy cheek.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.82>The gods withhold me!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.83>Shall I do that which all the Parthian darts,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.84>Though enemy, lost aim, and could not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.85>Eros,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.86>Wouldst thou be window'd in great Rome and see</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.87>Thy master thus with pleach'd arms, bending down</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.88>His corrigible neck, his face subdued</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.89>To penetrative shame, whilst the wheel'd seat</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.90>Of fortunate Caesar, drawn before him, branded</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.91>His baseness that ensued?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.92>I would not see't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.93>Come, then; for with a wound I must be cured.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.94>Draw that thy honest sword, which thou hast worn</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.95>Most useful for thy country.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.96>O, sir, pardon me!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.97>When I did make thee free, sworest thou not then</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.98>To do this when I bade thee? Do it at once;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.99>Or thy precedent services are all</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.100>But accidents unpurposed. Draw, and come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.101>Turn from me, then, that noble countenance,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.102>Wherein the worship of the whole world lies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.103>Lo thee!</p>
<p><i>Turning from him</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.104>My sword is drawn.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.105>                  Then let it do at once</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.106>The thing why thou hast drawn it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.107>My dear master,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.108>My captain, and my emperor, let me say,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.109>Before I strike this bloody stroke, farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.110>'Tis said, man; and farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.111>Farewell, great chief. Shall I strike now?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.112>Now, Eros.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>EROS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.113>Why, there then: thus I do escape the sorrow</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.114>Of Antony's death.</p>
<p><i>Kills himself</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.115>                  Thrice-nobler than myself!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.116>Thou teachest me, O valiant Eros, what</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.117>I should, and thou couldst not. My queen and Eros</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.118>Have by their brave instruction got upon me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.119>A nobleness in record: but I will be</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.120>A bridegroom in my death, and run into't</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.121>As to a lover's bed. Come, then; and, Eros,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.122>Thy master dies thy scholar: to do thus</p>
<p><i>Falling on his sword</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.123>I learn'd of thee. How! not dead? not dead?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.124>The guard, ho! O, dispatch me!</p>
<p><i>Enter DERCETAS and Guard</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.125>What's the noise?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.126>I have done my work in, friends: O, make an end</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.127>Of what I have begun.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>Second Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.128>The star is fall'n.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.129>And time is at his period.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.130>Alas, and woe!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.131>Let him that loves me strike me dead.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.132>Not I.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>Second Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.133>Nor I.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>Third Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.134>Nor any one.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Guard</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>DERCETAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.135>Thy death and fortunes bid thy followers fly.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.136>This sword but shown to Caesar, with this tidings,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.137>Shall enter me with him.</p>
<p><i>Enter DIOMEDES</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.138>Where's Antony?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>DERCETAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.139>                  There, Diomed there.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.140>Lives he?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.141>Wilt thou not answer, man?</p>
<p><i>Exit DERCETAS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.142>Art thou there, Diomed? Draw thy sword, and give me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.143>Sufficing strokes for death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.144>Most absolute lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.145>My mistress Cleopatra sent me to thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.146>When did she send thee?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.147>Now, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.148>Where is she?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.149>Lock'd in her monument. She had a prophesying fear</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.150>Of what hath come to pass: for when she saw--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.151>Which never shall be found--you did suspect</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.152>She had disposed with Caesar, and that your rage</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.153>Would not be purged, she sent you word she was dead;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.154>But, fearing since how it might work, hath sent</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.155>Me to proclaim the truth; and I am come,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.156>I dread, too late.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.157>Too late, good Diomed: call my guard, I prithee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.158>What, ho, the emperor's guard! The guard, what, ho!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.159>Come, your lord calls!</p>
<p><i>Enter four or five of the Guard of MARK ANTONY</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.160>Bear me, good friends, where Cleopatra bides;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.161>'Tis the last service that I shall command you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.162>Woe, woe are we, sir, you may not live to wear</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.163>All your true followers out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.164>Most heavy day!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.14.165>Nay, good my fellows, do not please sharp fate</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.166>To grace it with your sorrows: bid that welcome</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.167>Which comes to punish us, and we punish it</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.168>Seeming to bear it lightly. Take me up:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.169>I have led you oft: carry me now, good friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.14.170>And have my thanks for all.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt, bearing MARK ANTONY</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE XV. The same. A monument.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA and her maids aloft, with CHARMIAN and IRAS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.1>O Charmian, I will never go from hence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.2>Be comforted, dear madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.3>No, I will not:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.4>All strange and terrible events are welcome,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.5>But comforts we despise; our size of sorrow,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.6>Proportion'd to our cause, must be as great</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.7>As that which makes it.</p>
<p><i>Enter, below, DIOMEDES</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.8>How now! is he dead?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DIOMEDES</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.9>His death's upon him, but not dead.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.10>Look out o' the other side your monument;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.11>His guard have brought him thither.</p>
<p><i>Enter, below, MARK ANTONY, borne by the Guard</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.12>O sun,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.13>Burn the great sphere thou movest in!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.14>darkling stand</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.15>The varying shore o' the world. O Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.16>Antony, Antony! Help, Charmian, help, Iras, help;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.17>Help, friends below; let's draw him hither.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.18>Peace!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.19>Not Caesar's valour hath o'erthrown Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.20>But Antony's hath triumph'd on itself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.21>So it should be, that none but Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.22>Should conquer Antony; but woe 'tis so!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.23>I am dying, Egypt, dying; only</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.24>I here importune death awhile, until</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.25>Of many thousand kisses the poor last</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.26>I lay up thy lips.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.27>                  I dare not, dear,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.28>Dear my lord, pardon,--I dare not,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.29>Lest I be taken: not the imperious show</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.30>Of the full-fortuned Caesar ever shall</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.31>Be brooch'd with me; if knife, drugs,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.32>serpents, have</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.33>Edge, sting, or operation, I am safe:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.34>Your wife Octavia, with her modest eyes</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.35>And still conclusion, shall acquire no honour</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.36>Demuring upon me. But come, come, Antony,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.37>Help me, my women,--we must draw thee up:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.38>Assist, good friends.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.39>O, quick, or I am gone.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.40>Here's sport indeed! How heavy weighs my lord!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.41>Our strength is all gone into heaviness,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.42>That makes the weight: had I great Juno's power,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.43>The strong-wing'd Mercury should fetch thee up,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.44>And set thee by Jove's side. Yet come a little,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.45>Wishes were ever fools,--O, come, come, come;</p>
<p><i>They heave MARK ANTONY aloft to CLEOPATRA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.46>And welcome, welcome! die where thou hast lived:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.47>Quicken with kissing: had my lips that power,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.48>Thus would I wear them out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.49>A heavy sight!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.50>I am dying, Egypt, dying:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.51>Give me some wine, and let me speak a little.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.52>No, let me speak; and let me rail so high,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.53>That the false housewife Fortune break her wheel,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.54>Provoked by my offence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.55>One word, sweet queen:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.56>Of Caesar seek your honour, with your safety. O!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.57>They do not go together.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.58>Gentle, hear me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.59>None about Caesar trust but Proculeius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.60>My resolution and my hands I'll trust;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.61>None about Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MARK ANTONY</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.62>The miserable change now at my end</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.63>Lament nor sorrow at; but please your thoughts</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.64>In feeding them with those my former fortunes</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.65>Wherein I lived, the greatest prince o' the world,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.66>The noblest; and do now not basely die,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.67>Not cowardly put off my helmet to</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.68>My countryman,--a Roman by a Roman</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.69>Valiantly vanquish'd. Now my spirit is going;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.70>I can no more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.71>                  Noblest of men, woo't die?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.72>Hast thou no care of me? shall I abide</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.73>In this dull world, which in thy absence is</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.74>No better than a sty? O, see, my women,</p>
<p><i>MARK ANTONY dies</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.75>The crown o' the earth doth melt. My lord!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.76>O, wither'd is the garland of the war,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.77>The soldier's pole is fall'n: young boys and girls</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.78>Are level now with men; the odds is gone,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.79>And there is nothing left remarkable</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.80>Beneath the visiting moon.</p>
<p><i>Faints</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.81>O, quietness, lady!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.82>She is dead too, our sovereign.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.83>Lady!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.84>Madam!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.85>O madam, madam, madam!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.86>Royal Egypt, Empress!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.87>Peace, peace, Iras!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.15.88>No more, but e'en a woman, and commanded</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.89>By such poor passion as the maid that milks</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.90>And does the meanest chares. It were for me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.91>To throw my sceptre at the injurious gods;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.92>To tell them that this world did equal theirs</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.93>Till they had stol'n our jewel. All's but naught;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.94>Patience is scottish, and impatience does</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.95>Become a dog that's mad: then is it sin</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.96>To rush into the secret house of death,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.97>Ere death dare come to us? How do you, women?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.98>What, what! good cheer! Why, how now, Charmian!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.99>My noble girls! Ah, women, women, look,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.100>Our lamp is spent, it's out! Good sirs, take heart:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.101>We'll bury him; and then, what's brave,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.102>what's noble,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.103>Let's do it after the high Roman fashion,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.104>And make death proud to take us. Come, away:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.105>This case of that huge spirit now is cold:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.106>Ah, women, women! come; we have no friend</p>
<p class="line" name=4.15.107>But resolution, and the briefest end.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt; those above bearing off MARK ANTONY's body</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT V</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Alexandria. OCTAVIUS CAESAR's camp.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, AGRIPPA, DOLABELLA, MECAENAS, GALLUS, PROCULEIUS, and others, his council of war</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.1>Go to him, Dolabella, bid him yield;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.2>Being so frustrate, tell him he mocks</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.3>The pauses that he makes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.4>Caesar, I shall.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Enter DERCETAS, with the sword of MARK ANTONY</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.5>Wherefore is that? and what art thou that darest</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.6>Appear thus to us?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>DERCETAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.7>                  I am call'd Dercetas;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.8>Mark Antony I served, who best was worthy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.9>Best to be served: whilst he stood up and spoke,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.10>He was my master; and I wore my life</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.11>To spend upon his haters. If thou please</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.12>To take me to thee, as I was to him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.13>I'll be to Caesar; if thou pleasest not,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.14>I yield thee up my life.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.15>What is't thou say'st?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>DERCETAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.16>I say, O Caesar, Antony is dead.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.17>The breaking of so great a thing should make</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.18>A greater crack: the round world</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.19>Should have shook lions into civil streets,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.20>And citizens to their dens: the death of Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.21>Is not a single doom; in the name lay</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.22>A moiety of the world.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>DERCETAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.23>He is dead, Caesar:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.24>Not by a public minister of justice,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.25>Nor by a hired knife; but that self hand,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.26>Which writ his honour in the acts it did,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.27>Hath, with the courage which the heart did lend it,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.28>Splitted the heart. This is his sword;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.29>I robb'd his wound of it; behold it stain'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.30>With his most noble blood.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.31>Look you sad, friends?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.32>The gods rebuke me, but it is tidings</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.33>To wash the eyes of kings.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.34>And strange it is,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.35>That nature must compel us to lament</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.36>Our most persisted deeds.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.37>His taints and honours</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.38>Waged equal with him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>AGRIPPA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.39>A rarer spirit never</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.40>Did steer humanity: but you, gods, will give us</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.41>Some faults to make us men. Caesar is touch'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MECAENAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.42>When such a spacious mirror's set before him,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.43>He needs must see himself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.44>O Antony!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.45>I have follow'd thee to this; but we do lance</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.46>Diseases in our bodies: I must perforce</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.47>Have shown to thee such a declining day,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.48>Or look on thine; we could not stall together</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.49>In the whole world: but yet let me lament,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.50>With tears as sovereign as the blood of hearts,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.51>That thou, my brother, my competitor</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.52>In top of all design, my mate in empire,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.53>Friend and companion in the front of war,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.54>The arm of mine own body, and the heart</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.55>Where mine his thoughts did kindle,--that our stars,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.56>Unreconciliable, should divide</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.57>Our equalness to this. Hear me, good friends--</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.58>But I will tell you at some meeter season:</p>
<p><i>Enter an Egyptian</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.59>The business of this man looks out of him;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.60>We'll hear him what he says. Whence are you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Egyptian</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.61>A poor Egyptian yet. The queen my mistress,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.62>Confined in all she has, her monument,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.63>Of thy intents desires instruction,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.64>That she preparedly may frame herself</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.65>To the way she's forced to.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.66>Bid her have good heart:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.67>She soon shall know of us, by some of ours,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.68>How honourable and how kindly we</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.69>Determine for her; for Caesar cannot live</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.70>To be ungentle.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>Egyptian</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.71>So the gods preserve thee!</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.72>Come hither, Proculeius. Go and say,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.73>We purpose her no shame: give her what comforts</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.74>The quality of her passion shall require,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.75>Lest, in her greatness, by some mortal stroke</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.76>She do defeat us; for her life in Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.77>Would be eternal in our triumph: go,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.78>And with your speediest bring us what she says,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.79>And how you find of her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.80>Caesar, I shall.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.81>Gallus, go you along.</p>
<p><i>Exit GALLUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.82>Where's Dolabella,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.83>To second Proculeius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.84>Dolabella!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.85>Let him alone, for I remember now</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.86>How he's employ'd: he shall in time be ready.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.87>Go with me to my tent; where you shall see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.88>How hardly I was drawn into this war;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.89>How calm and gentle I proceeded still</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.90>In all my writings: go with me, and see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.91>What I can show in this.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. Alexandria. A room in the monument.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CLEOPATRA, CHARMIAN, and IRAS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.1>My desolation does begin to make</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.2>A better life. 'Tis paltry to be Caesar;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.3>Not being Fortune, he's but Fortune's knave,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.4>A minister of her will: and it is great</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.5>To do that thing that ends all other deeds;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.6>Which shackles accidents and bolts up change;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.7>Which sleeps, and never palates more the dug,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.8>The beggar's nurse and Caesar's.</p>
<p><i>Enter, to the gates of the monument, PROCULEIUS, GALLUS and Soldiers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.9>Caesar sends greeting to the Queen of Egypt;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.10>And bids thee study on what fair demands</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.11>Thou mean'st to have him grant thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.12>What's thy name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.13>My name is Proculeius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.14>Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.15>Did tell me of you, bade me trust you; but</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.16>I do not greatly care to be deceived,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.17>That have no use for trusting. If your master</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.18>Would have a queen his beggar, you must tell him,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.19>That majesty, to keep decorum, must</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.20>No less beg than a kingdom: if he please</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.21>To give me conquer'd Egypt for my son,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.22>He gives me so much of mine own, as I</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.23>Will kneel to him with thanks.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.24>Be of good cheer;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.25>You're fall'n into a princely hand, fear nothing:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.26>Make your full reference freely to my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.27>Who is so full of grace, that it flows over</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.28>On all that need: let me report to him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.29>Your sweet dependency; and you shall find</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.30>A conqueror that will pray in aid for kindness,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.31>Where he for grace is kneel'd to.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.32>Pray you, tell him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.33>I am his fortune's vassal, and I send him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.34>The greatness he has got. I hourly learn</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.35>A doctrine of obedience; and would gladly</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.36>Look him i' the face.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.37>This I'll report, dear lady.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.38>Have comfort, for I know your plight is pitied</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.39>Of him that caused it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>GALLUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.40>You see how easily she may be surprised:</p>
<p><i>Here PROCULEIUS and two of the Guard ascend the  monument by a ladder placed against a window, and,  having descended, come behind CLEOPATRA. Some of the Guard unbar and open the gates</i></p>
<p><i>To PROCULEIUS and the Guard</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.41>Guard her till Caesar come.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.42>Royal queen!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.43>O Cleopatra! thou art taken, queen:</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.44>Quick, quick, good hands.</p>
<p><i>Drawing a dagger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.45>Hold, worthy lady, hold:</p>
<p><i>Seizes and disarms her</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.46>Do not yourself such wrong, who are in this</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.47>Relieved, but not betray'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.48>What, of death too,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.49>That rids our dogs of languish?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.50>Cleopatra,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.51>Do not abuse my master's bounty by</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.52>The undoing of yourself: let the world see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.53>His nobleness well acted, which your death</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.54>Will never let come forth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.55>Where art thou, death?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.56>Come hither, come! come, come, and take a queen</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.57>Worthy many babes and beggars!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.58>O, temperance, lady!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.59>Sir, I will eat no meat, I'll not drink, sir;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.60>If idle talk will once be necessary,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.61>I'll not sleep neither: this mortal house I'll ruin,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.62>Do Caesar what he can. Know, sir, that I</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.63>Will not wait pinion'd at your master's court;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.64>Nor once be chastised with the sober eye</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.65>Of dull Octavia. Shall they hoist me up</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.66>And show me to the shouting varletry</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.67>Of censuring Rome? Rather a ditch in Egypt</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.68>Be gentle grave unto me! rather on Nilus' mud</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.69>Lay me stark naked, and let the water-flies</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.70>Blow me into abhorring! rather make</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.71>My country's high pyramides my gibbet,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.72>And hang me up in chains!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.73>You do extend</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.74>These thoughts of horror further than you shall</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.75>Find cause in Caesar.</p>
<p><i>Enter DOLABELLA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.76>Proculeius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.77>What thou hast done thy master Caesar knows,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.78>And he hath sent for thee: for the queen,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.79>I'll take her to my guard.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>PROCULEIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.80>So, Dolabella,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.81>It shall content me best: be gentle to her.</p>
<p><i>To CLEOPATRA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.82>To Caesar I will speak what you shall please,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.83>If you'll employ me to him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.84>Say, I would die.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt PROCULEIUS and Soldiers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.85>Most noble empress, you have heard of me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.86>I cannot tell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.87>                  Assuredly you know me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.88>No matter, sir, what I have heard or known.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.89>You laugh when boys or women tell their dreams;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.90>Is't not your trick?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.91>I understand not, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.92>I dream'd there was an Emperor Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.93>O, such another sleep, that I might see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.94>But such another man!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.95>If it might please ye,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.96>His face was as the heavens; and therein stuck</p>
