<p class="line" name=5.2.97>A sun and moon, which kept their course,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.98>and lighted</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.99>The little O, the earth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.100>Most sovereign creature,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.101>His legs bestrid the ocean: his rear'd arm</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.102>Crested the world: his voice was propertied</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.103>As all the tuned spheres, and that to friends;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.104>But when he meant to quail and shake the orb,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.105>He was as rattling thunder. For his bounty,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.106>There was no winter in't; an autumn 'twas</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.107>That grew the more by reaping: his delights</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.108>Were dolphin-like; they show'd his back above</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.109>The element they lived in: in his livery</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.110>Walk'd crowns and crownets; realms and islands were</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.111>As plates dropp'd from his pocket.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.112>Cleopatra!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.113>Think you there was, or might be, such a man</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.114>As this I dream'd of?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.115>Gentle madam, no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.116>You lie, up to the hearing of the gods.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.117>But, if there be, or ever were, one such,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.118>It's past the size of dreaming: nature wants stuff</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.119>To vie strange forms with fancy; yet, to imagine</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.120>And Antony, were nature's piece 'gainst fancy,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.121>Condemning shadows quite.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.122>Hear me, good madam.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.123>Your loss is as yourself, great; and you bear it</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.124>As answering to the weight: would I might never</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.125>O'ertake pursued success, but I do feel,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.126>By the rebound of yours, a grief that smites</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.127>My very heart at root.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.128>I thank you, sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.129>Know you what Caesar means to do with me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.130>I am loath to tell you what I would you knew.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.131>Nay, pray you, sir,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.132>Though he be honourable,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.133>He'll lead me, then, in triumph?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.134>Madam, he will; I know't.</p>
<p><i>Flourish, and shout within, 'Make way there: Octavius Caesar!'</i></p>
<p><i>Enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR, GALLUS, PROCULEIUS, MECAENAS, SELEUCUS, and others of his Train</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.135>Which is the Queen of Egypt?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.136>It is the emperor, madam.</p>
<p><i>CLEOPATRA kneels</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.137>Arise, you shall not kneel:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.138>I pray you, rise; rise, Egypt.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.139>Sir, the gods</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.140>Will have it thus; my master and my lord</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.141>I must obey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.142>                  Take to you no hard thoughts:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.143>The record of what injuries you did us,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.144>Though written in our flesh, we shall remember</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.145>As things but done by chance.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.146>Sole sir o' the world,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.147>I cannot project mine own cause so well</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.148>To make it clear; but do confess I have</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.149>Been laden with like frailties which before</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.150>Have often shamed our sex.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.151>Cleopatra, know,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.152>We will extenuate rather than enforce:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.153>If you apply yourself to our intents,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.154>Which towards you are most gentle, you shall find</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.155>A benefit in this change; but if you seek</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.156>To lay on me a cruelty, by taking</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.157>Antony's course, you shall bereave yourself</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.158>Of my good purposes, and put your children</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.159>To that destruction which I'll guard them from,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.160>If thereon you rely. I'll take my leave.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.161>And may, through all the world: 'tis yours; and we,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.162>Your scutcheons and your signs of conquest, shall</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.163>Hang in what place you please. Here, my good lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.164>You shall advise me in all for Cleopatra.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.165>This is the brief of money, plate, and jewels,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.166>I am possess'd of: 'tis exactly valued;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.167>Not petty things admitted. Where's Seleucus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>SELEUCUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.168>Here, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.169>This is my treasurer: let him speak, my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.170>Upon his peril, that I have reserved</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.171>To myself nothing. Speak the truth, Seleucus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>SELEUCUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.172>Madam,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.173>I had rather seal my lips, than, to my peril,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.174>Speak that which is not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.175>What have I kept back?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>SELEUCUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.176>Enough to purchase what you have made known.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.177>Nay, blush not, Cleopatra; I approve</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.178>Your wisdom in the deed.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.179>See, Caesar! O, behold,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.180>How pomp is follow'd! mine will now be yours;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.181>And, should we shift estates, yours would be mine.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.182>The ingratitude of this Seleucus does</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.183>Even make me wild: O slave, of no more trust</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.184>Than love that's hired! What, goest thou back? thou shalt</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.185>Go back, I warrant thee; but I'll catch thine eyes,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.186>Though they had wings: slave, soulless villain, dog!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.187>O rarely base!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.188>                  Good queen, let us entreat you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.189>O Caesar, what a wounding shame is this,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.190>That thou, vouchsafing here to visit me,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.191>Doing the honour of thy lordliness</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.192>To one so meek, that mine own servant should</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.193>Parcel the sum of my disgraces by</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.194>Addition of his envy! Say, good Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.195>That I some lady trifles have reserved,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.196>Immoment toys, things of such dignity</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.197>As we greet modern friends withal; and say,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.198>Some nobler token I have kept apart</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.199>For Livia and Octavia, to induce</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.200>Their mediation; must I be unfolded</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.201>With one that I have bred? The gods! it smites me</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.202>Beneath the fall I have.</p>
<p><i>To SELEUCUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.203>Prithee, go hence;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.204>Or I shall show the cinders of my spirits</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.205>Through the ashes of my chance: wert thou a man,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.206>Thou wouldst have mercy on me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.207>Forbear, Seleucus.</p>
<p><i>Exit SELEUCUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.208>Be it known, that we, the greatest, are misthought</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.209>For things that others do; and, when we fall,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.210>We answer others' merits in our name,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.211>Are therefore to be pitied.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.212>Cleopatra,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.213>Not what you have reserved, nor what acknowledged,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.214>Put we i' the roll of conquest: still be't yours,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.215>Bestow it at your pleasure; and believe,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.216>Caesar's no merchant, to make prize with you</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.217>Of things that merchants sold. Therefore be cheer'd;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.218>Make not your thoughts your prisons: no, dear queen;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.219>For we intend so to dispose you as</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.220>Yourself shall give us counsel. Feed, and sleep:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.221>Our care and pity is so much upon you,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.222>That we remain your friend; and so, adieu.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.223>My master, and my lord!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.224>Not so. Adieu.</p>
<p><i>Flourish. Exeunt OCTAVIUS CAESAR and his train</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.225>He words me, girls, he words me, that I should not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.226>Be noble to myself: but, hark thee, Charmian.</p>
<p><i>Whispers CHARMIAN</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.227>Finish, good lady; the bright day is done,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.228>And we are for the dark.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.229>Hie thee again:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.230>I have spoke already, and it is provided;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.231>Go put it to the haste.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.232>Madam, I will.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter DOLABELLA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.233>Where is the queen?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.234>Behold, sir.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.235>Dolabella!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.236>Madam, as thereto sworn by your command,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.237>Which my love makes religion to obey,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.238>I tell you this: Caesar through Syria</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.239>Intends his journey; and within three days</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.240>You with your children will he send before:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.241>Make your best use of this: I have perform'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.242>Your pleasure and my promise.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.243>Dolabella,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.244>I shall remain your debtor.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.245>I your servant,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.246>Adieu, good queen; I must attend on Caesar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.247>Farewell, and thanks.</p>
<p><i>Exit DOLABELLA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.248>Now, Iras, what think'st thou?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.249>Thou, an Egyptian puppet, shalt be shown</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.250>In Rome, as well as I	mechanic slaves</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.251>With greasy aprons, rules, and hammers, shall</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.252>Uplift us to the view; in their thick breaths,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.253>Rank of gross diet, shall be enclouded,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.254>And forced to drink their vapour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.255>The gods forbid!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.256>Nay, 'tis most certain, Iras: saucy lictors</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.257>Will catch at us, like strumpets; and scald rhymers</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.258>Ballad us out o' tune: the quick comedians</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.259>Extemporally will stage us, and present</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.260>Our Alexandrian revels; Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.261>Shall be brought drunken forth, and I shall see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.262>Some squeaking Cleopatra boy my greatness</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.263>I' the posture of a whore.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.264>O the good gods!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.265>Nay, that's certain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>IRAS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.266>I'll never see 't; for, I am sure, my nails</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.267>Are stronger than mine eyes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.268>Why, that's the way</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.269>To fool their preparation, and to conquer</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.270>Their most absurd intents.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter CHARMIAN</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.271>Now, Charmian!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.272>Show me, my women, like a queen: go fetch</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.273>My best attires: I am again for Cydnus,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.274>To meet Mark Antony: sirrah Iras, go.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.275>Now, noble Charmian, we'll dispatch indeed;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.276>And, when thou hast done this chare, I'll give thee leave</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.277>To play till doomsday. Bring our crown and all.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.278>Wherefore's this noise?</p>
<p><i>Exit IRAS. A noise within</i></p>
<p><i>Enter a Guardsman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.279>Here is a rural fellow</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.280>That will not be denied your highness presence:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.281>He brings you figs.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.282>Let him come in.</p>
<p><i>Exit Guardsman</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.283>What poor an instrument</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.284>May do a noble deed! he brings me liberty.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.285>My resolution's placed, and I have nothing</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.286>Of woman in me: now from head to foot</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.287>I am marble-constant; now the fleeting moon</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.288>No planet is of mine.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter Guardsman, with Clown bringing in a basket</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.289>This is the man.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.290>Avoid, and leave him.</p>
<p><i>Exit Guardsman</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.291>Hast thou the pretty worm of Nilus there,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.292>That kills and pains not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.293>Truly, I have him: but I would not be the party</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.294>that should desire you to touch him, for his biting</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.295>is immortal; those that do die of it do seldom or</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.296>never recover.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech90><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.297>Rememberest thou any that have died on't?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech91><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.298>Very many, men and women too. I heard of one of</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.299>them no longer than yesterday: a very honest woman,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.300>but something given to lie; as a woman should not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.301>do, but in the way of honesty: how she died of the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.302>biting of it, what pain she felt: truly, she makes</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.303>a very good report o' the worm; but he that will</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.304>believe all that they say, shall never be saved by</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.305>half that they do: but this is most fallible, the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.306>worm's an odd worm.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech92><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.307>Get thee hence; farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech93><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.308>I wish you all joy of the worm.</p>
<p><i>Setting down his basket</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech94><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.309>Farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech95><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.310>You must think this, look you, that the worm will</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.311>do his kind.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech96><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.312>Ay, ay; farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech97><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.313>Look you, the worm is not to be trusted but in the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.314>keeping of wise people; for, indeed, there is no</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.315>goodness in worm.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech98><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.316>Take thou no care; it shall be heeded.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech99><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.317>Very good. Give it nothing, I pray you, for it is</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.318>not worth the feeding.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech100><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.319>Will it eat me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech101><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.320>You must not think I am so simple but I know the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.321>devil himself will not eat a woman: I know that a</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.322>woman is a dish for the gods, if the devil dress her</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.323>not. But, truly, these same whoreson devils do the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.324>gods great harm in their women; for in every ten</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.325>that they make, the devils mar five.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech102><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.326>Well, get thee gone; farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech103><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.327>Yes, forsooth: I wish you joy o' the worm.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter IRAS with a robe, crown,  & c</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech104><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.328>Give me my robe, put on my crown; I have</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.329>Immortal longings in me: now no more</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.330>The juice of Egypt's grape shall moist this lip:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.331>Yare, yare, good Iras; quick. Methinks I hear</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.332>Antony call; I see him rouse himself</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.333>To praise my noble act; I hear him mock</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.334>The luck of Caesar, which the gods give men</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.335>To excuse their after wrath: husband, I come:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.336>Now to that name my courage prove my title!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.337>I am fire and air; my other elements</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.338>I give to baser life. So; have you done?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.339>Come then, and take the last warmth of my lips.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.340>Farewell, kind Charmian; Iras, long farewell.</p>
<p><i>Kisses them. IRAS falls and dies</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.341>Have I the aspic in my lips? Dost fall?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.342>If thou and nature can so gently part,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.343>The stroke of death is as a lover's pinch,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.344>Which hurts, and is desired. Dost thou lie still?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.345>If thus thou vanishest, thou tell'st the world</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.346>It is not worth leave-taking.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech105><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.347>Dissolve, thick cloud, and rain; that I may say,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.348>The gods themselves do weep!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech106><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.349>This proves me base:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.350>If she first meet the curled Antony,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.351>He'll make demand of her, and spend that kiss</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.352>Which is my heaven to have. Come, thou</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.353>mortal wretch,</p>
<p><i>To an asp, which she applies to her breast</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.354>With thy sharp teeth this knot intrinsicate</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.355>Of life at once untie: poor venomous fool</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.356>Be angry, and dispatch. O, couldst thou speak,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.357>That I might hear thee call great Caesar ass</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.358>Unpolicied!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech107><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.359>          O eastern star!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech108><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.360>Peace, peace!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.361>Dost thou not see my baby at my breast,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.362>That sucks the nurse asleep?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech109><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.363>O, break! O, break!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech110><b>CLEOPATRA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.364>As sweet as balm, as soft as air, as gentle,--</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.365>O Antony!--Nay, I will take thee too.</p>
<p><i>Applying another asp to her arm</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.366>What should I stay--</p>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech111><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.367>In this vile world? So, fare thee well.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.368>Now boast thee, death, in thy possession lies</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.369>A lass unparallel'd. Downy windows, close;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.370>And golden Phoebus never be beheld</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.371>Of eyes again so royal! Your crown's awry;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.372>I'll mend it, and then play.</p>
<p><i>Enter the Guard, rushing in</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech112><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.373>Where is the queen?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech113><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.374>Speak softly, wake her not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech114><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.375>Caesar hath sent--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech115><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.376>                  Too slow a messenger.</p>
<p><i>Applies an asp</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.377>O, come apace, dispatch! I partly feel thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech116><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.378>Approach, ho! All's not well: Caesar's beguiled.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech117><b>Second Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.379>There's Dolabella sent from Caesar; call him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech118><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.380>What work is here! Charmian, is this well done?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech119><b>CHARMIAN</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.381>It is well done, and fitting for a princess</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.382>Descended of so many royal kings.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.383>Ah, soldier!</p>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter DOLABELLA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech120><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.384>How goes it here?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech121><b>Second Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.385>                  All dead.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech122><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.386>Caesar, thy thoughts</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.387>Touch their effects in this: thyself art coming</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.388>To see perform'd the dreaded act which thou</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.389>So sought'st to hinder.</p>
<p><i>Within  'A way there, a way for Caesar!'</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter OCTAVIUS CAESAR and all his train marching</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech123><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.390>O sir, you are too sure an augurer;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.391>That you did fear is done.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech124><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.392>Bravest at the last,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.393>She levell'd at our purposes, and, being royal,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.394>Took her own way. The manner of their deaths?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.395>I do not see them bleed.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech125><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.396>Who was last with them?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech126><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.397>A simple countryman, that brought her figs:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.398>This was his basket.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech127><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.399>Poison'd, then.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech128><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.400>O Caesar,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.401>This Charmian lived but now; she stood and spake:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.402>I found her trimming up the diadem</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.403>On her dead mistress; tremblingly she stood</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.404>And on the sudden dropp'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech129><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.405>O noble weakness!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.406>If they had swallow'd poison, 'twould appear</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.407>By external swelling: but she looks like sleep,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.408>As she would catch another Antony</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.409>In her strong toil of grace.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech130><b>DOLABELLA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.410>Here, on her breast,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.411>There is a vent of blood and something blown:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.412>The like is on her arm.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech131><b>First Guard</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.413>This is an aspic's trail: and these fig-leaves</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.414>Have slime upon them, such as the aspic leaves</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.415>Upon the caves of Nile.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech132><b>OCTAVIUS CAESAR</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.416>Most probable</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.417>That so she died; for her physician tells me</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.418>She hath pursued conclusions infinite</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.419>Of easy ways to die. Take up her bed;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.420>And bear her women from the monument:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.421>She shall be buried by her Antony:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.422>No grave upon the earth shall clip in it</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.423>A pair so famous. High events as these</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.424>Strike those that make them; and their story is</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.425>No less in pity than his glory which</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.426>Brought them to be lamented. Our army shall</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.427>In solemn show attend this funeral;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.428>And then to Rome. Come, Dolabella, see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.429>High order in this great solemnity.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
